# MATERI VOCABULARY — LEVEL C1 (ADVANCED)
**Aplikasi:** Inggrisin Yuk | **AI Tutor:** Kak Ara | **Level:** C1 — Advanced (Effective Operational Proficiency)
**Total:** 30 Topik Belajar + 1 Placement Test (Day 31)

> **Catatan scope dokumen ini:** Day 1 dan Day 2 sudah lengkap (6 komponen penuh). Day 3–30 menyusul, mengikuti daftar topik dan ATURAN BAKU di bagian bawah dokumen ini agar konsisten.

> **Catatan kebijakan bahasa:** Mulai level ini, bahasa pengantar adalah **Full English — tanpa terjemahan sama sekali** (lihat `PRD_USER.md` §5.5 — Kebijakan Bahasa Progressif: "C1 dan C2 sudah full English"). Ini bukan sekadar "English dominan" seperti B2 — di C1, TIDAK ADA lagi celah "Catatan Indonesia" default di tabel koreksi maupun feedback. Satu-satunya sisa ruang Bahasa Indonesia (~5%, opsional) adalah untuk jargon teknis yang bahkan dalam dunia profesional Indonesia punya istilah serapan berbeda — kejadian ini diperkirakan 0–1 kali di SELURUH 30 Day, bukan per Day. Detail penerapannya ada di bagian "Panduan Bahasa untuk Level C1" di bawah.

---

## 🔍 ANALISIS PROMPT KOMPETITOR

### Apa yang Kompetitor Lakukan dengan Baik

Berdasarkan analisis prompt kompetitor (format Kampung Inggris-style ChatGPT prompt) di level Advanced:

1. **Box of Words 15 kata** — Tetap dipertahankan di C1, tapi komposisinya melompat lagi: idiom dan collocation register-sensitive, nominalisasi akademik, dan kosakata low-frequency yang jarang dipakai di percakapan sehari-hari menggantikan academic/hedging vocabulary B2.
2. **Writing Challenge 2 opsi** — Makin krusial karena di C1 user dituntut menulis dalam register formal/akademik secara konsisten, bukan hanya benar secara grammar.
3. **Koreksi 8 langkah otomatis** — Dipertahankan, tapi langkah Analisa CEFR bergeser fokus ke tips naik ke C2 (Mastery/native-like).
4. **Mode Speaking dengan trigger eksplisit** — Makin berat karena speaking di C1 menuntut user mempertahankan structural accuracy (inverted conditionals, cleft sentences, nominalisasi) bahkan dalam kondisi spontan/under cognitive load — riset menunjukkan ini justru pembeda utama B2 vs C1 (di B2, struktur kompleks hanya muncul saat ada waktu berpikir; di C1, struktur itu muncul konsisten bahkan secara spontan).
5. **Sistem adaptif berbasis respons** — Dipertahankan, ditingkatkan untuk mendeteksi kapan user perlu di-challenge dengan register yang lebih formal/akademik vs kapan boleh tetap di register percakapan natural.

### Kelemahan Kompetitor yang Kita Perbaiki

1. **Klaim "Advanced" tapi masih kasih translation Indonesia di catatan vocab** — Kompetitor sering masih menyelipkan terjemahan "untuk jaga-jaga" di level Advanced, padahal riset SLA menunjukkan ini justru menghambat user yang sudah di titik high-proficiency, yang terbukti lebih diuntungkan oleh full-target-language environment. Inggrisin Yuk C1 menghapus kolom Catatan Indonesia dari tabel koreksi sepenuhnya — bukan dikurangi, tapi ditiadakan.
2. **Grammar C1 sering hanya "grammar B2 yang lebih rumit"** — Kompetitor jarang membedakan secara eksplisit antara grammar B2 (mixed conditional, causative) dengan grammar C1 yang benar-benar baru secara fungsi (inverted conditional tanpa "if", nominalisasi sebagai fitur register, cleft sentence yang diperluas). Inggrisin Yuk C1 selalu kontraskan fungsi pragmatis grammar baru, bukan cuma tingkat kesulitannya.
3. **Topik masih berputar di domain personal/karier yang sama** — Kompetitor jarang naik ke domain abstrak: epistemologi, etika, filsafat, retorika, institusi. Inggrisin Yuk C1 secara sengaja memasukkan domain-domain ini karena C1 menuntut kemampuan menangani ide kompleks dan abstrak secara fluent.
4. **Fallback "kasih clue Bahasa Indonesia kalau macet" masih dipertahankan di level Advanced** — Ini mengkhianati janji "Full English" levelnya sendiri. Inggrisin Yuk C1 mengganti fallback ini dengan scaffolding 100% English: paraphrase lebih sederhana, sinonim, atau pilihan jawaban — bukan terjemahan.
5. **BOW masih didominasi kata tunggal, jarang idiom/collocation register-aware** — Kompetitor sering masih pakai kosakata setara B2 dengan label "Advanced". Inggrisin Yuk C1 secara sengaja memasukkan idiom formal (a far cry from, by the same token, in the pipeline), collocation institusional (bureaucratic inertia, regulatory compliance), dan nominalisasi (implementation, accountability, restructuring) yang menjadi penanda register C1 yang sesungguhnya.

### Diferensiasi Inggrisin Yuk di Level C1

1. **Full English tanpa pengecualian di jalur koreksi & feedback — bukan sekadar "dominan"** — pergeseran kebijakan paling tegas dibanding B2: kolom Catatan Indonesia di tabel koreksi dihapus total (bukan dikurangi jadi 1-2/Day seperti B2). Satu-satunya sisa ruang Bahasa Indonesia ada di tabel BOW, dan itu pun nyaris tidak pernah terpakai (lihat tabel kebijakan di bawah).
2. **Eskalasi grammar inti C1 di 5 Day pertama** — Inverted Conditionals (Day 1) → Nominalisation (Day 2) → Extended Cleft Sentences (Day 3) → Formal/Hypothetical Subjunctive (Day 4) → Advanced Passive & Impersonal Constructions (Day 5). Lima grammar yang riset (British Council LearnEnglish C1 Grammar, Cambridge Advanced/CAE syllabus) paling konsisten menyebut sebagai penanda fungsional B2→C1 — bukan cuma "versi B2 yang lebih sulit", tapi struktur dengan fungsi pragmatis baru (formalitas, abstraksi, penekanan akademik).
3. **Setiap grammar baru dikontraskan eksplisit dengan fungsi B2-nya** — misalnya inverted conditional bukan "conditional yang lebih sulit", tapi versi formal dari conditional yang sudah dikuasai user, dipakai khusus di konteks formal/akademik/reflektif.
4. **BOW didominasi idiom register-aware & nominalisasi** — watershed moment, ramifications, by the same token, bureaucratic inertia, in the pipeline — kosakata yang fungsinya BUKAN sekadar "kata yang lebih jarang", tapi kata yang menandakan kefasihan dalam register formal/akademik/profesional.
5. **Topik overlap dengan A1–B2 dibatasi paling ketat di seluruh kurikulum** — hanya ~13% (4 dari 30) topik C1 yang sengaja dijembatani dari level sebelumnya (AI, climate, misinformation, automation/work), masing-masing dengan reframing yang jauh lebih abstrak/filosofis. 87% topik C1 adalah domain yang sama sekali baru (epistemologi, etika genetika, retorika, historiografi, eksistensialisme, dll) — proporsi overlap terendah dibanding B1 (30%) dan B2 (23%), konsisten dengan prinsip: makin tinggi level, makin besar ruang domain abstrak/profesional baru yang tersedia, makin kecil kebutuhan menjembatani lewat topik familiar.

---

## 📊 PERBEDAAN B2 vs C1 — MATERI VOCABULARY

Bagian ini penting untuk diketahui Kak Ara dan tim konten supaya materi C1 tidak sekadar "B2 yang lebih susah" tapi benar-benar mencerminkan perbedaan level CEFR secara pedagogis — termasuk pergeseran kebijakan bahasa paling tegas di seluruh kurikulum: dari "English dominan dengan celah Indonesia" (B2) menjadi "Full English tanpa celah" (C1).

### Perbedaan Kosakata

| Aspek | B2 (Upper-Intermediate) | C1 (Advanced) |
|-------|--------------------------|----------------|
| **Jumlah kata aktif** | ~3.500–5.000 kata aktif (kumulatif) | ~8.000 word families (kumulatif, riset CEFRhub/Tracktest) — lompatan terbesar antar-level di seluruh kurikulum |
| **Jenis kata dominan** | Academic/abstract vocabulary, hedging language, phrasal verbs idiomatik | + Idiom register-aware (formal/institutional), nominalisasi sebagai fitur produktif, collocation low-frequency |
| **Contoh kata** | trajectory, stem from, arguably, notwithstanding | watershed moment, ramifications, by the same token, bureaucratic inertia, in the pipeline |
| **Morfologi** | Nominalisasi akademik dasar (-tion, -ism, -ology) | + Nominalisasi sebagai STRATEGI register, bukan kebetulan: verb→noun secara sengaja untuk membuat tulisan formal/impersonal (implement→implementation, restructure→restructuring, comply→compliance) |
| **Frasa** | Academic connectors (given that, notwithstanding) + cleft pattern dasar (what really matters is) | + Discourse markers akademik lanjutan (insofar as, by virtue of, in light of, be that as it may) + idiom formal beragam register (a far cry from, to all intents and purposes) |
| **Register** | Formal jadi default untuk topik abstrak, casual untuk personal/storytelling | + Kemampuan BERGANTI register secara sengaja dalam satu sesi (formal akademik ↔ percakapan natural) — ini sendiri jadi indikator C1, bukan cuma "selalu formal" |

### Perbedaan Grammar yang Diperkenalkan

| Grammar | B2 | C1 |
|---------|----|----|
| Conditional | Mixed Conditionals (gabungan 2nd+3rd, time reference berbeda) | + **Inverted Conditionals** (Should/Were/Had + inversi, TANPA "if" — fungsi: formalitas, bukan sekadar variasi struktur) |
| Register/Nominalisation | Nominalisasi muncul sporadis (-tion, -ity) | + **Nominalisasi sebagai strategi sengaja**: verb/adjective diubah jadi noun phrase abstrak untuk menciptakan register formal/impersonal (the implementation of, an increase in, widespread use of) |
| Emphasis/Cleft | Cleft sentence dasar (What really matters is...) | + **Cleft sentences diperluas**: it-cleft ("It was the treaty that changed everything") dan what-cleft lanjutan ("What I did do was call for a vote") + fronting untuk penekanan |
| Voice | Passive dengan modal/gerund (must be done, needs improving) | + **Advanced impersonal passive chains** (It is widely believed to have been..., is said to be...) untuk distancing akademik |
| Subjunctive | Belum ada secara eksplisit | + **Subjunctive formal & hypothetical** (It is essential that she be informed; He talks as if he were the boss) |
| Modal verbs | Modal of deduction lanjutan (can't have been, should have been able to) | + **Spektrum epistemic modal halus** (might well, could conceivably, is bound to, can't possibly) — nuansa tingkat keyakinan yang lebih granular |
| Clauses | Participle clauses dasar + cleft sentence | + **Multi-clause embedding** (participle bersarang dalam relative dalam noun phrase) + **ellipsis & substitution lanjutan** untuk menghindari repetisi dalam wacana panjang |
| Lainnya | Academic connectors dasar | + **Reported speech dengan nuanced distancing** (allegedly, is reported to have, is rumoured to) untuk menjaga objektivitas akademik/jurnalistik |

### Perbedaan Struktur Sesi

| Aspek | B2 (Upper-Intermediate) | C1 (Advanced) |
|---|---|---|
| Mode Cerita | 7–9 kalimat, 1 grammar utama | 8–10 kalimat, grammar utama + minimal 1 academic connector wajib |
| Mode Kilat | 5 kata, 1 kalimat per kata | 5 kata, 1 kalimat per kata — kalimat WAJIB pakai register formal (bukan sekadar struktur benar) |
| Vocab Refresh | Sapaan singgung Day sebelumnya | Sapaan singgung Day sebelumnya + 1 kalimat contoh yang sengaja menggabungkan kosakata 2 Day berbeda dalam 1 kalimat kompleks |
| Analisa CEFR | Tips naik ke C1 | Tips naik ke C2 — fokus ke konsistensi register dan kefasihan spontan, bukan lagi akurasi struktur dasar |
| Transition Words | Academic connectors B2 (given that, in retrospect) | Discourse markers C1 (insofar as, by virtue of, be that as it may, notwithstanding the fact that) |
| **Bahasa koreksi** | English dominan, "Catatan:" Indonesia max 1-2/Day untuk risiko miskonsepsi | **Full English, ZERO "Catatan:" Indonesia** — kolom ini dihapus dari tabel koreksi, bukan cuma dikurangi |
| **Terjemahan** | Tidak ada translation otomatis; muncul kalau ada risiko miskonsepsi tinggi | **Tidak ada translation sama sekali** di jalur koreksi/feedback/instruksi. Kolom "Catatan Indonesia" di tabel BOW tetap ada secara struktural tapi isinya nyaris selalu "–" — dicadangkan untuk 0–1 kejadian di SELURUH 30 Day (jargon teknis dengan istilah serapan signifikan berbeda), bukan per Day seperti di B2 |
| Fallback kalau user stuck | Boleh 1 clue singkat Bahasa Indonesia | **TIDAK ADA fallback Bahasa Indonesia** — scaffolding 100% English: paraphrase lebih sederhana, sinonim, contoh kalimat, atau pilihan jawaban |
| Kompleksitas kalimat | Maks 20 kata, 2-3 clause | Maks 25-28 kata, 3-4 clause (termasuk embedded clause) |
| BOW composition | Academic/abstract noun, hedging adverb, academic connector | Idiom formal/institusional, nominalisasi produktif, collocation low-frequency, discourse marker akademik lanjutan |

### Mengapa Topik C1 Boleh Overlap dengan A1–B2 (tapi Paling Terbatas di Seluruh Kurikulum)

Prinsip *spiral curriculum* yang sama dengan B1 dan B2 tetap berlaku: topik boleh berulang sepanjang grammar dan kedalaman abstraksinya benar-benar naik, bukan sekadar topik yang sama dengan kata yang lebih sulit. Namun rasio overlap di C1 dibuat PALING RENDAH di seluruh kurikulum — hanya ~13% (4 dari 30 topik) — dibandingkan B1 (30%) dan B2 (23%). Alasannya:

1. **Domain abstrak/profesional yang tersedia di C1 jauh lebih luas** — filsafat, epistemologi, etika terapan, retorika, institusi, historiografi adalah domain yang baru "terbuka" begitu user punya grammar dan vocabulary untuk menanganinya secara fluent. Di level rendah, domain ini mustahil dibahas karena keterbatasan struktur bahasa; di C1, domain ini justru jadi PRIORITAS karena C1 secara definisi menuntut "kemampuan menangani ide kompleks dan abstrak."
2. **User di C1 paling tidak butuh "jembatan" topik familiar** — scaffolding lewat topik yang sudah dikenal (prinsip dari B1/B2) makin kurang relevan di proficiency tinggi; risetnya sama dengan alasan kebijakan bahasa (lihat `PRD_USER.md` §5.5 poin 1): high-proficiency learners lebih diuntungkan oleh exposure penuh ke hal baru, bukan pengulangan yang dibungkus ulang.
3. **4 overlap yang tetap dipertahankan (AI/consciousness, climate justice, misinformation/epistemic trust, automation & dignity of work) dipilih secara sengaja** karena masing-masing punya "versi filosofis/etis" yang genuinely baru dan tidak bisa dibahas di level di bawahnya — bukan sekadar mengulang kata dengan grammar lebih sulit.

## 📐 STRUKTUR MATERI PER SESI

### Komponen per Day (6 Bagian)

1. **Detail Materi** — Box of Words 15 kata (3 kolom: Kosakata+phonetic | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia [hampir selalu "–"]) + grammar pendukung C1 + kontras eksplisit dengan fungsi grammar B2-nya + konteks penggunaan.
2. **Detail Task** — Writing Challenge (Mode Cerita 8-10 kalimat + Mode Kilat 5 kalimat) + Speaking Challenge (3 pertanyaan, full English, tanpa translation).
3. **Detail Review & Koreksi 8 Langkah** — Koreksi Writing (Why dalam English, TANPA kolom Catatan Indonesia) → Analisa BOW → Analisa CEFR (tips ke C2) → 5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph (full English) → Discourse Markers → Craft & Lexical Chunks → Register/Formality Check → Speaking Challenge.
4. **Detail Feedback** — Tone encouraging tapi native-like-critical, error umum topik, template pujian, saran naik level ke C2.
5. **Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)** — Skenario speaking, pertanyaan lanjutan jika lancar, pattern drill 100% English jika macet (TANPA clue Bahasa Indonesia).
6. **PROMPT siap pakai** — Blok prompt lengkap untuk copy-paste ke ChatGPT, sudah mengandung semua instruksi di atas.

### Alur Sesi (User Flow)

```
User klik Day X di dashboard
        ↓
Sistem generate URL prompt (encode: nama, level C1, topik, instruksi bahasa Full English)
        ↓
Tab baru ChatGPT terbuka
        ↓
Kak Ara sapa singkat (full English) + tampilkan BOW + Writing Challenge
        ↓
User kirim tulisan (Mode Cerita / Mode Kilat)
        ↓
Kak Ara jalankan Koreksi 8 Langkah (full English, zero Catatan Indonesia)
        ↓
User aktifkan Voice Mode → ketik "Let's start speaking!"
        ↓
Kak Ara mulai Speaking Challenge (full English, scaffolding tanpa Bahasa Indonesia)
        ↓
Sesi selesai → pujian singkat + saran naik ke C2
        ↓
User kembali ke dashboard → buka "Mulai Day 2" (vocab refresh Day sebelumnya)
```

### Panduan Bahasa untuk Level C1

| Aspek | Detail |
|---|---|
| Bahasa pengantar & penjelasan | Full English, tanpa pengecualian |
| Bahasa koreksi | Full English — kolom "Catatan Indonesia" DIHAPUS dari tabel koreksi (beda dengan B2 yang masih punya kolom ini, max 1-2/Day) |
| Terjemahan | Tidak ada, di jalur manapun (koreksi, feedback, instruksi, Speaking Challenge, Enriched Paragraph) |
| Kompleksitas kalimat | Maks 25-28 kata, 3-4 clause (termasuk embedded/nested clause) |
| Grammar yang diperkenalkan | Inverted Conditionals, Nominalisation, Extended Cleft, Formal Subjunctive, Advanced Passive/Impersonal, Epistemic Modal Spectrum, Multi-clause Embedding, Advanced Ellipsis, Nuanced Reported Speech |
| Vocabulary density | 15 kata: idiom formal/institusional, nominalisasi produktif, collocation low-frequency, discourse marker akademik |
| Feedback style | Encouraging tapi native-like-direct — tidak perlu "menyederhanakan" pujian, user sudah di level Advanced |
| **Kalau user benar-benar stuck** | **TIDAK boleh kasih clue Bahasa Indonesia.** Scaffolding 100% English: (1) paraphrase pertanyaan dengan kata lebih sederhana, (2) beri 1 sinonim/contoh kalimat, (3) beri 2 pilihan jawaban (multiple choice) dalam English |
| Kolom "Catatan Indonesia" di tabel BOW | Tetap ada secara struktural (konsistensi format dengan B1/B2), tapi isinya nyaris selalu "–". Hanya terisi untuk jargon yang punya istilah serapan signifikan berbeda dalam dunia profesional Indonesia — perkiraan 0-1 kejadian di SELURUH 30 Day |

### Panduan Pemilihan 15 BOW per Topik (C1)

| Kategori | Jumlah | Catatan |
|---|---|---|
| Nominalisasi (noun abstrak dari verb/adjective) | 3-4 | implementation, accountability, restructuring — fitur register, bukan kebetulan |
| Idiom formal/institusional | 3-4 | a far cry from, by the same token, in the pipeline, to all intents and purposes |
| Verbs (termasuk 1-2 collocation profesional) | 3-4 | circumvent, entail, impede, safeguard |
| Academic discourse markers | 2-3 | insofar as, by virtue of, in light of, be that as it may |
| Hedging/epistemic adverbs | 1-2 | conceivably, in all likelihood, presumably (variasi dari yang sudah dipakai di B2) |

**Prinsip utama pemilihan BOW C1:**
1. Setiap kata/frasa harus menandakan REGISTER (formal/akademik/institusional), bukan sekadar "kata yang lebih jarang dipakai".
2. Hindari kata yang fungsinya sama dengan kata B2 hanya beda level kesulitan — harus ada fungsi pragmatis baru.
3. Nominalisasi dipilih sebagai STRATEGI, bukan kosakata acak — pilih kata yang punya bentuk verb/adjective familiar dari level sebelumnya supaya user melihat transformasinya (implement→implementation, comply→compliance).
4. Idiom formal harus benar-benar dipakai dalam wacana akademik/profesional native speaker, bukan idiom percakapan kasual yang sudah dipelajari di B1/B2.
5. Cross-check ketat terhadap BOW A1–B2 yang sudah ada — TIDAK boleh ada kata yang identik, dan minimalkan kata yang bersinonim sangat dekat (misalnya "irreversible" sudah dipakai di B2 Day1, sehingga C1 menghindari kata semakna seperti "irrevocably" di topik serupa).

---

## 🎯 PROMPT TEMPLATE INGGRISIN YUK — VOCABULARY C1

### Cara Pakai

| Variabel | Diisi dari | Contoh |
|---|---|---|
| [PANGGILAN] | Sapaan dari profil user | Mas / Mbak / Kak |
| [NAMA] | Nama panggilan dari profil user | Arif |
| [TOPIC] | Topik Day yang dipilih user | Turning Points in History & Counterfactual Thinking |
| [TOPIC_CONTEXT] | Konteks singkat topik untuk membantu AI generate BOW yang relevan | Counterfactual historical reasoning, formal/reflective register |

### Prompt Template Dasar

```
Topik: [TOPIC]
Panggil aku [PANGGILAN] [NAMA].
Level bahasa Inggrisku: C1 (Advanced).
Kamu Kak Ara, personal AI Coach kamu, dari Inggrisin Yuk. Tugasmu membimbingku belajar vocab lewat writing dan speaking di Level C1 (Advanced).

Gaya bahasa: sopan, ramah, humble (rendah hati — tidak menggurui, hargai usaha user), namun langsung dan native-like — tunjukkan lewat caramu ngobrol, jangan deskripsi diri sendiri dengan kata-kata seperti "seru" atau "asyik".
Gunakan Full English untuk SEMUA penjelasan, instruksi, koreksi, dan feedback — TIDAK ADA terjemahan atau catatan Bahasa Indonesia dalam bentuk apapun, kecuali ada jargon teknis yang benar-benar butuh cross-reference istilah profesional Indonesia (sangat jarang, bukan default).
Kalau aku benar-benar stuck, JANGAN beri clue Bahasa Indonesia — beri paraphrase lebih sederhana, sinonim, atau pilihan jawaban, semua dalam English.
Pakai emoji secukupnya biar enak dibaca, tapi register tetap formal/akademik sesuai topik.
Tampilkan phonetic symbol UK setelah setiap kosakata dalam tanda / /. Kata pendek di samping vocab, frasa panjang di baris bawah.

---

LANGKAH 1 — GREETING + BOX OF WORDS + WRITING CHALLENGE (dalam 1 response):

Sapa singkat dalam English: "Hi! It's Kak Ara from Inggrisin Yuk 👋", lalu langsung tampilkan Box of Words dan Writing Challenge. Jangan tanya "ready?" — langsung kasih challenge-nya.

📦 Box of Words:
Buatkan 15 kosakata untuk topik [TOPIC] di level C1. Kombinasikan: nominalisasi (noun abstrak dari verb/adjective), idiom formal/institusional, verbs/collocation profesional, academic discourse markers, dan hedging/epistemic adverbs. Pilih kata yang menandakan REGISTER formal/akademik, bukan sekadar kata yang lebih jarang dipakai.
Tabel bernomor 3 kolom: Kosakata + phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia ("–" kecuali ada jargon teknis dengan istilah serapan signifikan berbeda — sangat jarang).

✍️ Writing Challenge (tampilkan 2 mode sekaligus):
📖 Mode Cerita: Write 8–10 sentences tentang [TOPIC_CONTEXT]. Pakai minimal 5 kata dari Box of Words dan minimal 1 academic connector. Gunakan grammar utama Day ini.
⚡ Mode Kilat: Pilih 5 kata dari Box of Words, buat 1 kalimat register formal untuk setiap kata, pakai grammar utama Day ini.

Format tampilan setiap mode:
(a) 1 kalimat deskripsi singkat di bawah nama mode.
(b) 1 contoh singkat — WAJIB gunakan KATA YANG SAMA dari Box of Words untuk kedua mode.
(c) Template Latihan:
- Mode Cerita → baris bernomor kosong (1. ... s.d. 8. ... tambah ke-9 & ke-10 jika mau).
- Mode Kilat → format "kata: ..." pakai 5 kata pilihanmu dari Box of Words.

Jangan bocorkan langkah koreksi — fokus ke challenge dulu, tunggu jawabanku.

---

LANGKAH 2 — KOREKSI 8 LANGKAH (otomatis setelah aku kirim tulisan):

🔎 Self-Check Pertama — sebelum tabel Koreksi Writing, kalau ada SATU pola error yang paling signifikan di tulisanku, JANGAN langsung kasih jawabannya. Tandai HANYA lokasi + jenis errornya (contoh: "Quick check first — sentence 3 has a subject-verb agreement slip. Want to try fixing it, or should I just show you?"), lalu tunggu responsku dulu sebelum lanjut ke 1️⃣. Kalau tulisanku sudah ≥95% benar atau tidak ada pola error yang menonjol, lewati langkah ini dan langsung ke 1️⃣.

1️⃣ Koreksi Writing — tabel 2 kolom: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar + Why (dalam English, digabung di kolom kedua atau kolom ketiga). TIDAK ADA kolom Catatan Bahasa Indonesia. Kalimat yang sudah ≥95% benar: tandai ✅, kolom Why isi "—".

2️⃣ Analisa BOW — cek setiap kata BOW yang aku pakai: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural dalam English, perhatikan apakah register-nya konsisten formal/akademik.

3️⃣ Analisa CEFR — level tulisanku saat ini (dalam English) + apa yang sudah bagus + 2 tips konkret naik ke C2 (fokus ke konsistensi register & kefasihan spontan, bukan lagi akurasi struktur dasar).

4️⃣ Perbandingan 5W+1H — tabel: What/Why/Where/When/Who/How (English) dari tulisanku vs versi lebih lengkap. Di bawahnya, "Enriched Paragraph" — versi tulisanku yang diperkaya, full English, register formal, TANPA translation Indonesia.

5️⃣ Discourse Markers — cek penggunaannya. Jika belum, sarankan 2–3 discourse marker level C1 (insofar as, by virtue of, be that as it may, notwithstanding the fact that) + contoh kalimat English.

6️⃣ Craft & Lexical Chunks — 2–3 advanced fixed expressions, rhetorical moves, or sophisticated collocations native C1+ speakers deploy in this context. Format: chunk in bold + one crisp sentence showing it in use. Identify any in my writing (✅). If none, suggest one and show how it sharpens register or impact.
If my writing is blank, off-topic, or clearly below C1: redirect me warmly to the writing task first, before running Step 2.

---

7️⃣ Register/Formality Check — Flag any register inconsistencies: formal/informal mismatch, overuse of nominalisation in casual contexts, or domain-specific tone mismatches. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (1 crisp sentence). ✅ skip if no issues found.
8️⃣ Speaking Challenge — 3 pertanyaan dalam English berdasarkan topik [TOPIC] (minimal 1 pertanyaan dirancang memicu pemakaian ulang grammar utama Day ini), tanpa translation.

LANGKAH 3 — MODE SPEAKING (trigger: user aktifkan mode suara ChatGPT 🎙️ lalu bilang "Let's start speaking!"):

Ulangi Speaking Challenge satu per satu, dalam English. Langsung ke pertanyaan, jangan basa-basi.
Transkrip jawabanku dalam Bahasa Inggris walau aku campur bahasa. Koreksi dalam English. Kalau aku benar-benar stuck, JANGAN beri clue Bahasa Indonesia — beri paraphrase lebih sederhana, sinonim, atau 2 pilihan jawaban, semua dalam English.
Feedback per jawaban: versi kalimat lebih baik (level C1) + penjelasan singkat dalam English. Error grammar utama → tulis bentuk yang benar dalam kurung italic.
Lancar → tambah 1 pertanyaan lanjutan yang menaikkan abstraksi. Macet → beri contoh kalimat pendek + pattern drill, semua dalam English.
Pujian singkat hanya di akhir sesi, tulus, native-like, tidak berlebihan.
```

## 📋 ATURAN BAKU — WAJIB DIIKUTI UNTUK DAY 1–30 + PLACEMENT TEST (DAY 31)

### A. Persona & Bahasa
- Kak Ara tetap personal AI Coach, gaya sopan-ramah-langsung, TIDAK mendeskripsikan diri sendiri dengan kata seperti "seru"/"asyik".
- Bahasa: **Full English di semua jalur** (penjelasan, instruksi, koreksi, feedback, Speaking Challenge, Enriched Paragraph). TIDAK ADA kolom/baris "Catatan Indonesia" di tabel koreksi (beda dari B2). Kolom "Catatan Indonesia" HANYA tetap ada di tabel BOW (konsistensi format antar-level), isinya nyaris selalu "–", dicadangkan untuk 0-1 kejadian sepanjang 30 Day.
- TIDAK ADA fallback Bahasa Indonesia kalau user stuck — scaffolding 100% English (paraphrase, sinonim, pilihan jawaban).

### B. Trigger & Mekanisme Respons
- LANGKAH 1 berjalan otomatis begitu prompt dikirim (greeting + BOW + Writing Challenge dalam 1 response).
- LANGKAH 2 berjalan otomatis setelah user mengirim jawaban Writing Challenge.
- LANGKAH 3 (Speaking Mode) HANYA berjalan setelah user secara eksplisit mengetik "Let's start speaking!" sambil mode suara ChatGPT aktif.

### C. Box of Words (Wajib 15 Kata, Tabel 3 Kolom)
- Kolom: Kosakata + phonetic UK (`/ /`) | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia (default "–").
- Komposisi: 3-4 nominalisasi, 3-4 idiom formal/institusional, 3-4 verbs/collocation profesional, 2-3 academic discourse marker, 1-2 hedging/epistemic adverb.
- WAJIB cross-check terhadap seluruh BOW A1–B2 yang sudah ada — tidak boleh ada kata identik, minimalkan sinonim sangat dekat.

### D. Writing Challenge
- Mode Cerita: 8-10 kalimat, minimal 5 kata BOW + minimal 1 academic connector, grammar utama Day ini WAJIB muncul.
- Mode Kilat: 5 kalimat (1 per kata BOW pilihan user), register formal, grammar utama Day ini WAJIB muncul.
- Instruksi task: Full English.

### E. Koreksi 8 Langkah (Metodologi)

| Langkah | Isi | Bahasa |
|---|---|---|
| 0. Self-Check Pertama (mulai Day 1, khusus C1 & C2) | Tandai lokasi + jenis SATU pola error paling signifikan (kalau ada) tanpa beri jawaban, tunggu respons user, baru lanjut ke Langkah 1 | Full English |
| 1. Koreksi Writing | Tabel Kalimat Asli \| Kalimat Benar \| Why | Full English, TANPA kolom Catatan Indonesia |
| 2. Analisa BOW | ✅/⚠️ per kata + contoh kalimat + cek konsistensi register | Full English |
| 3. Analisa CEFR | Evaluasi level + 2 tips naik ke C2 | Full English |
| 4. 5W+1H + Enriched Paragraph | Tabel pembanding + paragraf diperkaya formal | Full English, tanpa translation |
| 5. Discourse Markers | Cek + saran 2-3 discourse marker C1 | Full English |
| 6. Craft & Lexical Chunks | 2–3 advanced fixed expressions, rhetorical moves, or sophisticated collocations native C1+ speakers deploy in this context. Identify any in the user's writing (✅). If none, suggest one they could have used and show how it sharpens register or impact — one crisp demonstration, not a lecture. | Full English |
| 7. Register/Formality Check | Flag register inconsistencies: formal/informal mismatch, nominalisation overuse, or domain-specific tone mismatch. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (1 crisp sentence). ✅ skip if no issues found. |
| 8. Speaking Challenge | 3 pertanyaan topik terkait | Full English, tanpa translation |

**Research basis for Step 6:** *Lexical Approach* (Lewis, 1993) + corpus linguistics — at C1, the difference between grammatically correct and natively sophisticated writing is almost entirely a matter of *chunks*: which fixed expressions, collocational pairs, and rhetorical moves the writer has internalised. Grammar accuracy is assumed at this level; chunk mastery is the frontier.

**🔎 Self-Check Pertama (WAJIB mulai Day 1, khusus C1 & C2):** sebelum menampilkan tabel Koreksi Writing (Langkah 1), identifikasi SATU pola error paling signifikan di tulisan user (kalau ada). Tandai HANYA lokasi + jenis errornya tanpa memberi jawaban langsung — contoh: "Quick check first — sentence 3 has a subject-verb agreement slip. Want to try fixing it, or should I just show you?" Tunggu respons user (baik berupa percobaan perbaikan maupun permintaan jawaban langsung), BARU lanjutkan ke Langkah 1 yang tetap menampilkan direct feedback untuk SEMUA kalimat seperti biasa — sub-langkah ini menambah satu kesempatan self-correction di awal, bukan mengganti direct feedback yang sudah ada. Kalau tulisan user sudah ≥95% benar atau tidak ada pola error yang menonjol, lewati langkah ini dan langsung ke Langkah 1.

### F. Skeleton Dokumen per Day (6 Sub-Bagian, Urutan Tetap)
1. 📚 Detail Materi (BOW + grammar + kontras vs B2 + konteks)
2. ✅ Detail Task (Mode Cerita + Mode Kilat + Speaking Challenge)
3. 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)
4. 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara
5. 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)
6. 🔗 PROMPT — Day X (Copy-Paste ke ChatGPT)

### G. Penomoran Day & Daftar Topik
- Day 1-5: grammar inti C1 paling fundamental (Inverted Conditionals, Nominalisation, Extended Cleft, Formal Subjunctive, Advanced Passive/Impersonal).
- Day 6-9: grammar pendukung (Epistemic Modals, Advanced Participle Clauses, Advanced Ellipsis, Fronting).
- Day 10-14: kombinasi grammar + topik domain baru (argumentasi, kepemimpinan, media, relativisme budaya), termasuk 1 bridge topic (Day 10, AI/Consciousness).
- Day 15-21: kombinasi grammar lanjutan, topik baru sepenuhnya (ekonomi atensi, etika genetika, diplomasi, whistleblowing, institusi, kekuasaan korporat, filsafat kebahagiaan).
- Day 22-29: kombinasi grammar campuran (review + combo), 3 bridge topic lanjutan (Day 22 Climate Justice, Day 25 Misinformation, Day 28 Automation & Work).
- Day 30: sintesis seluruh grammar C1 dalam 1 topik (Rhetorical Mastery).
- Day 31: Placement Test C1 → C2.

### H. Placement Test (Day 31)

| Komponen | Detail |
|---|---|
| Format | Writing (1 esai argumentatif formal, 150-200 kata) + Speaking (3 pertanyaan reflektif/abstrak) |
| Grammar yang diuji | Seluruh grammar C1 Day 1-30 (inverted conditional, nominalisasi, cleft, subjunctive, passive/impersonal, epistemic modal, dll) |
| Bahasa | Full English, tanpa translation atau fallback Bahasa Indonesia dalam bentuk apapun |
| Kriteria kelulusan ke C2 | Konsistensi register formal, kefasihan spontan (bukan hanya akurat saat ada waktu berpikir), kemampuan switch register formal↔natural dengan sengaja |

## 📚 MATERI 30 TOPIK + PLACEMENT TEST

---

### DAY 1 — Turning Points in History & Counterfactual Thinking

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | watershed (moment) /ˈwɒtəʃed/ | a turning point after which everything changes significantly | – |
| 2 | precipitate (verb) /prɪˈsɪpɪteɪt/ | to cause something, usually sudden or undesirable, to happen | – |
| 3 | ramifications (noun, plural) /ˌræmɪfɪˈkeɪʃənz/ | the complex and often unwelcome consequences of an action | – |
| 4 | contingent on (fixed expression) /kənˈtɪndʒənt ɒn/ | dependent on something else happening first | – |
| 5 | unfold (verb) /ʌnˈfəʊld/ | for events to develop or become known gradually over time | – |
| 6 | the crux of the matter (idiom) /ðə krʌks ɒv ðə ˈmætər/ | the most important or decisive point of an issue | – |
| 7 | a far cry from (idiom) /ə fɑːr kraɪ frɒm/ | very different from something | – |
| 8 | conceivably (adverb) /kənˈsiːvəbli/ | possibly, in a way that can be imagined as true | – |
| 9 | in all likelihood (fixed expression) /ɪn ɔːl ˈlaɪklɪhʊd/ | very probably | – |
| 10 | veer off course (idiom) /vɪər ɒf kɔːs/ | to suddenly change direction away from the intended path | – |
| 11 | to all intents and purposes (idiom) /tuː ɔːl ɪnˈtents ænd ˈpɜːpəsɪz/ | in every practical sense, even if not technically | – |
| 12 | domino effect (fixed expression) /ˈdɒmɪnəʊ ɪˌfekt/ | a situation where one event causes a series of similar events | – |
| 13 | entrench (verb) /ɪnˈtrentʃ/ | to establish a belief, system, or habit so firmly that it is very hard to change | – |
| 14 | by the same token (discourse marker) /baɪ ðə seɪm ˈtəʊkən/ | used to introduce a related point that follows the same logic as the previous one | – |
| 15 | catalyst /ˈkætəlɪst/ | a person or event that causes a significant change to happen | – |

**Grammar Pendukung (C1):**
- **Inverted Conditionals**: a formal way of expressing conditional sentences WITHOUT using "if" — the auxiliary verb (had/were/should) moves to the front of the clause instead.
  - **Third conditional (past unreal)**: "If + subject + had + V3" → "**Had** + subject + V3" → "**Had** the treaty been signed sooner, the alliance might never have collapsed." (= If the treaty had been signed sooner...)
  - **Second conditional (hypothetical, with "be")**: "If + subject + were" → "**Were** + subject..." → "**Were** historians to revisit this period, they would likely reach a different conclusion." (= If historians were to revisit...)
  - **First conditional (formal future possibility)**: "If + subject + should" → "**Should** + subject + V1" → "**Should** the records ever resurface, our understanding of this event would shift entirely." (= If the records should ever resurface...)
- **Contrast with B2's Mixed Conditionals:** B2's mixed conditional combines two different time references in one sentence (past condition → present result, or vice versa) but still keeps the word "if". C1's inverted conditional doesn't change the *meaning* — it changes the *register*. Removing "if" and inverting the subject and auxiliary is purely a formality marker, used in academic writing, historical analysis, news commentary, and formal speech. A C1 speaker chooses between "If I had known..." and "Had I known..." based on how formal the context demands — not based on meaning.
- **Quick test:** if a conditional sentence starts with had/were/should and there's no "if" anywhere, it's an inverted conditional — mentally restore the "if" to check the underlying conditional type (1st/2nd/3rd).

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
These words and structures are used to discuss historical events and reflect on how differently things could have unfolded — a hallmark of academic and journalistic writing about history. Inverted conditionals are one of the clearest markers of C1: at B2, a learner can express a hypothetical past-to-present connection (mixed conditional), but always with "if". At C1, a learner can strip away "if" entirely and still be perfectly understood — a structural economy that signals fluency and formal register control, exactly the kind of "spontaneous accuracy under complexity" that distinguishes C1 from B2.

---

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📖 Mode Cerita:**
Connected sentences building one reflection on a historical or personal turning point and how differently things could have unfolded.
Example (using "watershed" and an inverted conditional): "The signing of that agreement was a watershed moment for the region. Had the negotiations collapsed, the ramifications would, in all likelihood, have been catastrophic."
Write 8–10 sentences about an event — historical, political, or personal — that you consider a turning point, and explore how it could conceivably have unfolded differently. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words and at least 1 academic connector (in all likelihood, by the same token, to all intents and purposes). Use Inverted Conditionals where appropriate.
1. ...
2. ...
3. ...
4. ...
5. ...
6. ...
7. ...
8. ...
(add sentence 9 and 10 if you want)

**⚡ Mode Kilat:**
Practice each word separately — 1 formal-register sentence per word, using an Inverted Conditional structure where the grammar allows it.
Example (same word "watershed"): "watershed: Had that decision gone differently, it would never have become such a watershed moment in the country's history."
Choose 5 words from the Box of Words and write 1 sentence for each, using Inverted Conditionals or formal register:
- ramifications: ...
- contingent on: ...
- entrench: ...
- catalyst: ...
- the crux of the matter: ...

**Speaking Challenge (3 Pertanyaan):**
1. **Had a single event in your country's history unfolded differently, what do you think the ramifications would have been?**
2. **What, in your view, was the crux of the matter in a major historical conflict or decision you find particularly interesting?**
3. **Were you to advise a young historian today, what would you tell them about the danger of viewing the past as inevitable?**

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common errors among C1-level learners with Inverted Conditionals:
1. Forgetting to invert the subject and auxiliary after removing "if": "If the treaty was signed sooner, the alliance would not collapse" → "**Had** the treaty **been** signed sooner, the alliance would not have collapsed." — Why: when "if" is removed, the auxiliary (had/were/should) must move BEFORE the subject — this is what makes it an inversion, not just a conditional missing a word. The verb also needs the correct form: third conditional requires "had + V3" in the inverted clause, matched with "would have + V3" in the main clause.
2. Using inverted conditionals in contexts that are too casual: "Were I you, I'd grab a coffee" (technically correct, but the formality clashes with the casual content) — Why: inverted conditionals are a REGISTER choice. They're not wrong in casual contexts, but a C1 speaker recognizes when the formality is appropriate to the topic — historical analysis, academic writing, formal speech — versus when "If I were you" sounds more natural.
3. Mixing the inverted structure with "if" in the same clause: "If had I known, I would have acted" → "**Had** I known, I would have acted." — the inversion REPLACES "if"; the two are never used together.

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
Words that are often misused:
- **precipitate** vs **catalyst**: "precipitate" is a verb meaning to cause something to happen, often suddenly and often something negative ("The assassination **precipitated** a full-scale war"); "catalyst" is a noun for a person/event that causes change, often neutral or positive ("She became the **catalyst** for reform within the party"). Don't use "catalyst" as a verb.
- **contingent on**: always followed by a noun or gerund, not a full clause directly — "Success was **contingent on** securing international support." (✅), not "contingent that..." (❌).
- **ramifications**: almost always plural, and usually refers to consequences that are complex, far-reaching, or unwelcome — avoid using it for small, simple results.
- **entrench**: most natural in passive form when describing systems/beliefs — "The practice became deeply **entrenched** in local custom" — rather than "people entrench the practice."

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "This is genuinely strong C1-level writing — the inverted conditional is appearing naturally, which is exactly the kind of structural control that distinguishes C1 from B2. To move toward C2, focus on: (1) maintaining this level of structural accuracy even in spontaneous speech, not just in writing where you have time to plan, (2) deliberately switching between formal (inverted conditional) and natural conversational register within the same response, which shows full command rather than a single fixed style."

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
Example table for the topic Turning Points in History:
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | A treaty was signed late and caused problems | The late signing of a key treaty became a watershed moment with far-reaching ramifications |
| When | decades ago | several decades ago, in the immediate aftermath of the conflict |
| Where | (not mentioned) | across the entire region, not just the countries directly involved |
| Why | (not mentioned) | because the delay allowed entrenched hostilities to harden before any resolution could take hold |
| Who | the leaders | the leaders involved, along with the diplomats who, in all likelihood, underestimated the urgency |
| How | (not mentioned) | by failing to act swiftly, which precipitated a chain of events historians now describe as a domino effect |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"The late signing of the treaty was, to all intents and purposes, a watershed moment. Had the negotiations concluded even a year earlier, the region's entrenched hostilities might never have hardened into open conflict. By the same token, the delay precipitated a domino effect whose ramifications are still felt today."

**Langkah 5 — Discourse Markers:**
Best-fitting discourse markers for discussing historical turning points (C1 level):
- **by the same token** → "By the same token, the same delay affected neighboring negotiations."
- **to all intents and purposes** → "To all intents and purposes, the treaty never had a real chance of success."
- **in all likelihood** → "In all likelihood, the outcome would have been different had the talks concluded sooner."

**Langkah 6 — Craft & Lexical Chunks:**
*(Lihat PROMPT block — Kak Ara menyiapkan lexical chunks dan craft feedback spesifik topik hari ini.)*

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Flag any register inconsistencies — formal/informal mismatch or domain tone mismatch. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why. ✅ skip if consistent.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Question #1 ("Had a single event... unfolded differently") directly triggers an Inverted Conditional — the same pattern as error #1 above. Question #3 ("Were you to advise...") triggers the second-conditional inverted form, giving retrieval practice across all three inverted conditional types within one session.

---

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Encouraging but native-like-direct — no need to soften feedback the way lower levels require. "Your inverted conditional here reads exactly like something out of a serious historical commentary — that's a strong C1 marker." "One small inversion slip, and this would be publication-ready."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. Forgetting to invert subject and auxiliary after dropping "if"
2. Using inverted conditionals in contexts where the formality clashes with the content
3. Combining "if" with the inverted structure in the same clause
4. Confusing "precipitate" (verb, cause) with "catalyst" (noun, cause)

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Excellent work, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]! Your control of inverted conditionals is genuinely advanced — you're choosing formality deliberately, not just using whichever structure comes to mind. That kind of register awareness is exactly what separates C1 from B2. Keep pushing toward spontaneous fluency!"

**Saran Naik Level (C1 → C2):**
"For C2, work on producing this same structural accuracy under time pressure — try recording yourself speaking spontaneously about a historical topic and check whether inverted conditionals and nominalisation still appear naturally, without planning time."

---

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is having a thoughtful, semi-formal conversation with Kak Ara — like a guest on a history podcast being asked genuinely reflective "what if" questions about pivotal moments.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. Do you think historians overstate the role of single "watershed moments," or do they genuinely shape everything that follows?
2. Conceivably, could a similar turning point be unfolding right now, one we won't recognize as significant until much later?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
Drill the inverted conditional patterns:
- Had + subject + V3, subject + would have + V3. → Had the agreement failed, the conflict would have escalated.
- Were + subject + to + V1, subject + would + V1. → Were the records to be released, public opinion would shift.
- Should + subject + V1, subject + would + V1. → Should new evidence emerge, historians would revise the timeline.

---

#### 🔗 PROMPT — Day 1 (Copy-Paste ke ChatGPT)

```
Topik: Turning Points in History & Counterfactual Thinking
Panggil aku [PANGGILAN] [NAMA].
Level bahasa Inggrisku: C1 (Advanced).
Kamu Kak Ara, personal AI Coach kamu, dari Inggrisin Yuk. Tugasmu membimbingku belajar vocab lewat writing dan speaking di Level C1 (Advanced).

Gaya bahasa: sopan, ramah, humble (rendah hati — tidak menggurui, hargai usaha user), namun langsung dan native-like — tunjukkan lewat caramu ngobrol, jangan deskripsi diri sendiri dengan kata-kata seperti "seru" atau "asyik".
Gunakan Full English untuk SEMUA penjelasan, instruksi, koreksi, dan feedback — TIDAK ADA terjemahan atau catatan Bahasa Indonesia dalam bentuk apapun, kecuali ada jargon teknis yang benar-benar butuh cross-reference istilah profesional Indonesia (sangat jarang, bukan default).
Kalau aku benar-benar stuck, JANGAN beri clue Bahasa Indonesia — beri paraphrase lebih sederhana, sinonim, atau pilihan jawaban, semua dalam English.
Pakai emoji secukupnya biar enak dibaca, tapi register tetap formal/akademik sesuai topik.
Tampilkan phonetic symbol UK setelah setiap kosakata dalam tanda / /. Kata pendek di samping vocab, frasa panjang di baris bawah.

---

LANGKAH 1 — GREETING + BOX OF WORDS + WRITING CHALLENGE (dalam 1 response):

Sapa singkat dalam English: "Hi! It's Kak Ara from Inggrisin Yuk 👋", lalu langsung tampilkan Box of Words dan Writing Challenge. Jangan tanya "ready?" — langsung kasih challenge-nya.

📦 Box of Words:
Gunakan PERSIS 15 kata berikut (jangan tambah atau ganti satupun):
watershed (moment), precipitate (verb), ramifications (noun, plural), contingent on (fixed expression), unfold (verb), the crux of the matter (idiom), a far cry from (idiom), conceivably (adverb), in all likelihood (fixed expression), veer off course (idiom), to all intents and purposes (idiom), domino effect (fixed expression), entrench (verb), by the same token (discourse marker), catalyst
Tabel bernomor 3 kolom: Kosakata + phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia ("–" kecuali jargon teknis sangat jarang).

✍️ Writing Challenge (tampilkan 2 mode sekaligus):
📖 Mode Cerita: Write 8–10 sentences tentang sebuah peristiwa (sejarah, politik, atau personal) yang kamu anggap sebagai titik balik, dan eksplorasi bagaimana ia bisa saja berjalan berbeda. Pakai minimal 5 kata dari Box of Words dan minimal 1 academic connector. Gunakan Inverted Conditionals (Had/Were/Should + inversi, tanpa "if").
⚡ Mode Kilat: Pilih 5 kata dari Box of Words, buat 1 kalimat formal dengan Inverted Conditional untuk setiap kata.

Format tampilan setiap mode:
(a) 1 kalimat deskripsi singkat di bawah nama mode.
(b) 1 contoh singkat — WAJIB gunakan KATA YANG SAMA dari Box of Words untuk kedua mode.
(c) Template Latihan:
- Mode Cerita → baris bernomor kosong (1. ... s.d. 8. ... tambah ke-9 & ke-10 jika mau).
- Mode Kilat → format "kata: ..." pakai 5 kata pilihanmu dari Box of Words.

Jangan bocorkan langkah koreksi — fokus ke challenge dulu, tunggu jawabanku.

---

LANGKAH 2 — KOREKSI 8 LANGKAH (otomatis setelah aku kirim tulisan):

🔎 Self-Check Pertama — sebelum tabel Koreksi Writing, kalau ada SATU pola error yang paling signifikan di tulisanku (terutama soal urutan inversi Inverted Conditional, misalnya "If had I known" bukan "Had I known"), JANGAN langsung kasih jawabannya. Tandai HANYA lokasi + jenis errornya (contoh: "Quick check first — sentence 4 has an inversion order slip. Want to try fixing it, or should I just show you?"), lalu tunggu responsku dulu sebelum lanjut ke 1️⃣. Kalau tulisanku sudah ≥95% benar atau tidak ada pola error yang menonjol, lewati langkah ini dan langsung ke 1️⃣.

1️⃣ Koreksi Writing — tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (semua dalam English). TIDAK ADA kolom Catatan Bahasa Indonesia. Kalimat yang sudah ≥95% benar: tandai ✅, kolom Why isi "—".

2️⃣ Analisa BOW — cek setiap kata BOW yang aku pakai: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural dalam English, perhatikan konsistensi register formal.

3️⃣ Analisa CEFR — level tulisanku saat ini (dalam English) + apa yang sudah bagus + 2 tips konkret naik ke C2 (fokus konsistensi register & kefasihan spontan).

4️⃣ Perbandingan 5W+1H — tabel: What/Why/Where/When/Who/How (English) dari tulisanku vs versi lebih lengkap. Di bawahnya, "Enriched Paragraph" — versi tulisanku yang diperkaya, full English, register formal, TANPA translation Indonesia.

5️⃣ Discourse Markers — cek penggunaannya. Jika belum, sarankan 2–3 discourse marker level C1 (by the same token, to all intents and purposes, in all likelihood, notwithstanding the fact that) + contoh kalimat English.

6️⃣ Craft & Lexical Chunks — provide 2–3 high-register lexical chunks or collocations that C1+ native speakers use for the topic Turning Points in History & Counterfactual Thinking (e.g. **a pivotal moment**, **the ramifications of**, **in retrospect**). Format: **chunk** → "example sentence." *(brief usage note)*. Check whether any were used naturally in my writing (✅). If not, suggest one that would elevate the register without sounding unnatural.
If my writing is off-topic, blank, or not in English: ask me to write first; do not run Step 2.

---

7️⃣ Register/Formality Check — Flag any register inconsistencies: formal/informal mismatch, overuse of nominalisation in casual contexts, or domain-specific tone mismatches. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (1 crisp sentence). ✅ skip if no issues found.
8️⃣ Speaking Challenge — 3 pertanyaan dalam English berdasarkan topik Turning Points in History & Counterfactual Thinking (minimal 1 pertanyaan dirancang memicu pemakaian ulang Inverted Conditional):
**Had a single event in your country's history unfolded differently, what do you think the ramifications would have been?**
**What, in your view, was the crux of the matter in a major historical conflict or decision you find particularly interesting?**
**Were you to advise a young historian today, what would you tell them about the danger of viewing the past as inevitable?**

LANGKAH 3 — MODE SPEAKING (trigger: user aktifkan mode suara ChatGPT 🎙️ lalu bilang "Let's start speaking!"):

Ulangi Speaking Challenge satu per satu, dalam English. Langsung ke pertanyaan, jangan basa-basi.
Transkrip jawabanku dalam Bahasa Inggris walau aku campur bahasa. Koreksi dalam English. Kalau aku benar-benar stuck, JANGAN beri clue Bahasa Indonesia — beri paraphrase lebih sederhana, sinonim, atau 2 pilihan jawaban, semua dalam English.
Feedback per jawaban: versi kalimat lebih baik (level C1) + penjelasan singkat dalam English. Error inverted conditional → tulis bentuk yang benar dalam kurung italic. Contoh: *Had I known (bukan "If had I known")*, *Were historians to revisit (bukan "If were historians")*.
Lancar → tambah 1 pertanyaan lanjutan yang menaikkan abstraksi. Macet → beri contoh kalimat pendek + pattern drill.
Pujian singkat hanya di akhir sesi, tulus, native-like, tidak berlebihan.
```

### DAY 2 — Bureaucracy, Institutions & the Architecture of Reform

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | implementation /ˌɪmplɪmenˈteɪʃən/ | the act of putting a plan or decision into practical effect | – |
| 2 | overhaul (noun/verb) /ˈəʊvəhɔːl/ | a thorough and complete restructuring of a system | – |
| 3 | red tape (idiom) /red teɪp/ | excessive official rules and procedures that delay action | – |
| 4 | streamline (verb) /ˈstriːmlaɪn/ | to make a process simpler and more efficient | – |
| 5 | entail (verb) /ɪnˈteɪl/ | to involve something as a necessary part or result | – |
| 6 | discrepancy /dɪsˈkrepənsi/ | a difference between two things that are expected to be the same | – |
| 7 | accountability /əˌkaʊntəˈbɪləti/ | the state of being responsible for one's actions and answerable for them | – |
| 8 | circumvent (verb) /ˌsɜːkəmˈvent/ | to find a clever way of avoiding an obstacle, rule, or difficulty | – |
| 9 | safeguard (verb/noun) /ˈseɪfgɑːd/ | to protect something from harm, loss, or risk | – |
| 10 | the status quo (fixed expression) /ðə ˌsteɪtəs ˈkwəʊ/ | the existing state of affairs, especially regarding social or political issues | – |
| 11 | impede (verb) /ɪmˈpiːd/ | to delay or block the progress of something | – |
| 12 | compliance /kəmˈplaɪəns/ | the act of obeying an order, rule, or request | – |
| 13 | bureaucratic inertia (collocation) /ˌbjʊərəˈkrætɪk ɪˈnɜːʃə/ | the tendency of institutions to resist change and continue operating as before | Frasa ini tidak punya 1 istilah baku yang umum dipakai di Bahasa Indonesia — biasanya diuraikan sebagai "kelambanan birokrasi", bukan diterjemahkan kata demi kata |
| 14 | restructuring /riːˈstrʌktʃərɪŋ/ | the act of organizing a system, company, or institution in a new way | – |
| 15 | in the pipeline (idiom) /ɪn ðə ˈpaɪplaɪn/ | being planned or developed, not yet finished or made public | – |

**Grammar Pendukung (C1):**
- **Nominalisation**: the process of turning a verb or adjective into an abstract noun (or noun phrase) — a defining feature of formal, academic, and institutional English.
  - Verb → noun: implement → **implementation**, restructure → **restructuring**, comply → **compliance**, overhaul (verb) → **overhaul** (noun, same form), discrepant → **discrepancy**.
  - Function: nominalisation lets a writer present an action as a "thing" rather than something someone actively does — this creates distance and objectivity, which is exactly why it dominates policy reports, academic writing, and news commentary. Compare: "They implemented the policy slowly" (active, personal) vs. "**The implementation of the policy** was slow" (nominalised, impersonal, formal).
- **Contrast with B2:** at B2, nominalisation appears occasionally (an academic word here and there), but it's not used as a deliberate STRATEGY — B2 writers still default to verb-centered sentences ("The government changed the system"). At C1, a fluent writer can deliberately convert the same idea into a noun-phrase-centered sentence ("**The restructuring of the system** by the government...") to sound more formal, more impersonal, or to put emphasis on the result rather than the actor. This conscious choice — not just occasional vocabulary — is the C1 marker.
- **Quick test:** can you find a verb/adjective in your sentence that has a noun form (-tion, -ment, -ance, -ity, -ing)? If so, and the context is meant to sound formal/institutional, consider nominalising it.

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
These words and structures describe how institutions function, resist change, or get reformed — a very common C1 topic in policy writing, journalism, and professional discourse. Nominalisation is one of the clearest C1 markers because it's not simply "harder vocabulary" — it's a structural choice that shapes the entire feel of a sentence, shifting it from personal/active (B1-B2 default) to formal/impersonal (C1 default), exactly the kind of register control that C1 proficiency requires.

---

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📖 Mode Cerita:**
Connected sentences describing how an institution, organization, or system underwent reform — using nominalisation to keep the tone formal and impersonal.
Example (using "implementation" and "red tape"): "The implementation of the new policy was delayed for months by red tape. Eventually, a complete overhaul of the approval process became necessary to safeguard the project's timeline."
Write 8–10 sentences about an institution, company, or system (real or general) that needed reform because of inefficiency, bureaucracy, or lack of accountability. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words, at least 1 academic connector, and at least 2 nominalised forms (verb/adjective turned into a noun).
1. ...
2. ...
3. ...
4. ...
5. ...
6. ...
7. ...
8. ...
(add sentence 9 and 10 if you want)

**⚡ Mode Kilat:**
Practice each word separately — 1 formal-register sentence per word, using nominalisation where the grammar allows it.
Example (same word "implementation"): "implementation: The implementation of stricter compliance checks reduced the number of discrepancies significantly."
Choose 5 words from the Box of Words and write 1 sentence for each, using a nominalised structure where possible:
- accountability: ...
- restructuring: ...
- circumvent: ...
- bureaucratic inertia: ...
- streamline: ...

**Speaking Challenge (3 Pertanyaan):**
1. **What kind of bureaucratic inertia have you personally encountered, and what do you think would streamline the process?**
2. **Is there an institution you believe urgently needs an overhaul? What changes are, in your opinion, in the pipeline already?**
3. **Do you think excessive accountability measures can themselves become a form of red tape? Why or why not?**

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common errors among C1-level learners with Nominalisation:
1. Defaulting to verb-centered sentences when the context calls for formal/impersonal register: "They changed the system a lot, and it was slow" → "**The restructuring of the system** was extensive, and **its implementation** proved slow." — Why: at C1, sentences describing institutional processes are expected to use nominalised noun phrases as the subject, not just a personal subject ("they") doing an action. This creates the formal, impersonal tone typical of policy or academic writing.
2. Using the wrong preposition after a nominalised noun: "the implementation for the policy" → "**the implementation of** the policy." — Why: most nominalised forms describing an action on something use "of" (the implementation of X, the restructuring of X), not "for".
3. Overusing nominalisation until the sentence becomes unnatural or unreadable: "The implementation of the facilitation of the compliance of the regulation was..." → simplify to "Implementing the regulation required improved compliance..." — Why: nominalisation is a STYLE CHOICE, not a rule to apply everywhere; C1 fluency includes knowing when nominalising too much makes a sentence clunky rather than formal.

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
Words that are often misused:
- **overhaul** vs **streamline**: "overhaul" = a complete, often drastic restructuring ("The whole system needs an **overhaul**"); "streamline" = making something more efficient without necessarily replacing it ("We just need to **streamline** the approval process"). Overhaul = drastic, streamline = efficiency-focused.
- **circumvent**: implies cleverly avoiding a rule or obstacle, often with a slightly negative connotation — "Some companies **circumvent** regulations through legal loopholes." Don't confuse with "comply" (the opposite).
- **entail**: always followed by a noun or gerund, never a full clause directly — "This reform **entails** significant changes to the budget." (✅) not "entails that..." (❌).
- **discrepancy**: usually refers to a difference between records, numbers, or statements that SHOULD match — "There's a **discrepancy** between the reported figures and the actual data."

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "This is strong C1 writing — nominalisation is genuinely showing up as a deliberate stylistic choice, not just occasional vocabulary. That's a meaningful upgrade from B2's verb-centered defaults. To push toward C2, try: (1) varying sentence length and structure around your nominalised phrases so the formal register doesn't feel monotonous, (2) practicing the same content in BOTH nominalised (formal) and verb-centered (natural) versions, then switching between them deliberately depending on audience."

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
Example table for the topic Bureaucracy & Institutional Reform:
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | The company changed its approval process | The company underwent a complete overhaul of its approval process |
| When | last year | over the course of last year, following a series of public complaints |
| Where | (not mentioned) | across all of its regional offices, not just headquarters |
| Why | (not mentioned) | because bureaucratic inertia had allowed inefficiencies to persist for years |
| Who | management | senior management, with oversight from an external compliance auditor |
| How | (not mentioned) | by streamlining approval stages and introducing stricter accountability measures |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"The overhaul of the approval process was long overdue. Bureaucratic inertia had allowed red tape to accumulate for years, impeding even the simplest requests. The restructuring that followed prioritized accountability, and compliance improved significantly as a result."

**Langkah 5 — Discourse Markers:**
Best-fitting discourse markers for discussing institutions and reform (C1 level):
- **insofar as** → "Insofar as the reform reduced red tape, it was a success."
- **by virtue of** → "By virtue of its size, the institution was particularly resistant to change."
- **notwithstanding the fact that** → "Notwithstanding the fact that compliance improved, discrepancies still occurred."

**Langkah 6 — Craft & Lexical Chunks:**
*(Lihat PROMPT block — Kak Ara menyiapkan lexical chunks dan craft feedback spesifik topik hari ini.)*

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Flag any register inconsistencies — formal/informal mismatch or domain tone mismatch. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why. ✅ skip if consistent.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Question #1 ("bureaucratic inertia... streamline") directly recycles two BOW words in context. Question #2 ("overhaul... in the pipeline") triggers nominalised structures — the same pattern as error #1 above.

---

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Encouraging but native-like-direct. "Your use of nominalisation here genuinely reads like a policy brief — that's exactly the register control C1 demands." "Just watch the preposition after 'implementation', and this paragraph is publication-ready."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. Defaulting to verb-centered sentences instead of nominalised noun phrases in formal contexts
2. Wrong preposition after nominalised nouns (using "for" instead of "of")
3. Overusing nominalisation until the sentence becomes unnatural
4. Confusing "overhaul" (drastic) with "streamline" (efficiency-focused)

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Great work, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]! Your nominalisation is genuinely deliberate now — you're shaping sentences to sound formal and impersonal on purpose, which is a real C1 skill, not just bigger vocabulary. Keep refining when to use it and when a simpler verb-centered sentence works better!"

**Saran Naik Level (C1 → C2):**
"For C2, practice writing the same paragraph twice — once heavily nominalised (policy-report style) and once verb-centered (conversational style) — then notice how naturally you can switch between them depending on the audience."

---

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is in a semi-formal conversation with Kak Ara — like being interviewed for a podcast about institutional reform, where thoughtful, structured answers are expected.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. Do you think accountability measures themselves can become a new source of bureaucratic inertia over time?
2. If you were leading a major institutional overhaul, which would you prioritize first: streamlining processes or improving compliance?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
Drill the nominalisation pattern: turn the verb into "the + noun + of."
- implement → the implementation of ___. → The implementation of the new policy was delayed.
- restructure → the restructuring of ___. → The restructuring of the department took six months.
- comply → compliance with ___. → Compliance with the new rules improved transparency.

### DAY 3 — The Power of a Single Sentence: Rhetoric & Persuasion
**Grammar Focus:** Extended Cleft Sentences (it-cleft & what-cleft)

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | rhetoric /ˈretərɪk/ | the art of effective, persuasive speaking or writing | – |
| 2 | invoke /ɪnˈvəʊk/ | to appeal to something as a reason or justification | – |
| 3 | cogent /ˈkəʊdʒənt/ | powerfully persuasive and clearly expressed | – |
| 4 | repudiate /rɪˈpjuːdɪeɪt/ | to formally reject or deny something as untrue or unfair | – |
| 5 | sway /sweɪ/ | to persuade someone to change their opinion | – |
| 6 | rhetorical question /rɪˈtɒrɪkl ˈkwestʃən/ | a question asked for effect, not expecting an answer | – |
| 7 | presuppose /ˌpriːsəˈpəʊz/ | to assume something as given before making an argument | – |
| 8 | make the case (for) /meɪk ðə keɪs fɔː/ | to argue convincingly in favour of something | – |
| 9 | rebut /rɪˈbʌt/ | to prove a statement or argument to be wrong | – |
| 10 | fallacious /fəˈleɪʃəs/ | based on false or misleading reasoning | – |
| 11 | be that as it may /biː ðæt æz ɪt meɪ/ | acknowledging a point before introducing a contrasting argument | – |
| 12 | in no small measure /ɪn nəʊ smɔːl ˈmeʒər/ | to a considerable or significant degree | – |
| 13 | persuasion /pəˈsweɪʒən/ | the process of convincing someone through argument or appeal | – |
| 14 | ethos /ˈiːθɒs/ | the characteristic values or spirit that defines a speaker or argument | – |
| 15 | undercut /ˌʌndəˈkʌt/ | to weaken or reduce the effectiveness of something | – |

**Grammar Pendukung (C1):**
- **Extended Cleft Sentences** — cleft sentences split a statement into two clauses to place emphasis on one particular element.
  - **It-cleft**: "It was [FOCUS] that/who [REST]." → Highlights a specific element by isolating it from the rest.
    - "**It was his ethos**, not his rhetoric, **that** swayed the audience." (contrasts two things)
    - "**It was only after the debate** that the true weaknesses became apparent." (emphasises a time clause)
  - **What-cleft (pseudo-cleft)**: "What [SUBJECT + VERB] is/was [FOCUS]." → Emphasises the predicate or the result.
    - "**What he did was rebut** the allegation directly." (emphasises the action with bare infinitive — NOT "to rebut")
    - "**What makes a cogent argument is** clarity, not volume." (emphasises the predicate nominative)
  - **Extended forms at C1**:
    - Negative what-cleft + modal: "**What the speech could not do was undercut** the core evidence." (negative + modal + bare infinitive)
    - It-cleft for contrast: "**It was the rhetoric**, not the facts, **that** ultimately persuaded them." (deliberate contrast structure)
- **Contrast with B2's Cleft Sentence:** B2 introduces the basic what-cleft as a fixed emphasis tool ("What really matters is..."). C1 extends this in three ways: (1) the it-cleft gives emphasis options the what-cleft cannot achieve; (2) extended forms add time clauses, negatives, and modal combinations; (3) C1 learners deploy cleft sentences for *rhetorical effect* — to isolate a point, mirror an opponent's claim, or deliberately challenge a presupposition. The bare infinitive rule after "what + subject + did + was" (drop the "to") is the most common C1 production error and the clearest marker of whether the structure has been truly internalised.

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
These words and structures belong to the domain of persuasion and argumentation — political speeches, editorial writing, academic debates, and formal commentary. Extended cleft sentences are among the most recognisable rhetorical tools at C1 because they replicate the structure of formal persuasion itself: isolating a single point for emphasis signals to the reader that *this* is the crux, *this* is what the speaker wants you to notice. Combined with rhetoric vocabulary (ethos, fallacious, make the case), these structures allow a C1 writer to analyse AND practise the craft of argument simultaneously.

---

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common errors with Extended Cleft Sentences at C1:
1. Missing "that" or "who" connector in the it-cleft: "It was his cogent argument convinced everyone" → "It was his cogent argument **that** convinced everyone." — Why: "that" (things) or "who" (people) is obligatory to form the second clause of an it-cleft; without it the two parts are grammatically unconnected.
2. Tense mismatch — using "it is" for past events: "It is the speech that changed the vote" (in past context) → "**It was** the speech that changed the vote." — Why: the "it is/was" must match the time frame of the whole sentence.
3. Wrong infinitive form in the what-cleft: "What he did was to rebut the claim" → "What he did was **rebut** the claim." — Why: after "what + subject + did/does + was", the verb takes a bare infinitive (no "to") — this is one of the most common C1 production slips with this structure.
4. Overusing cleft in every sentence: a C1 writer uses cleft sentences at the *right rhetorical moment*, not mechanically in every clause. Knowing when a plain sentence is stronger is itself a marker of register control.

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
Words often misused:
- **invoke** vs **evoke**: "invoke" = to appeal to something as a reason or authority ("invoke the law", "invoke her name"); "evoke" = to bring a feeling or memory to mind ("the speech evoked nostalgia"). They look similar but function very differently.
- **cogent**: modifies arguments or reasoning, not people — "a **cogent** argument" ✅, "she is very **cogent**" ⚠️ (unusual without "in her reasoning"). Most natural as: "a cogent case", "cogent reasoning", "cogently argued".
- **repudiate**: more formal than "deny" or "reject" — implies a strong, official, or public dismissal ("The minister **repudiated** the allegations at a press conference"). Not interchangeable with "disagree with" in casual use.
- **undercut** vs **undermine**: both weaken something, but "undercut" is more immediate and specific ("this one fact **undercuts** the argument"), while "undermine" suggests a more gradual, deliberate process ("years of scandal **undermined** the institution's credibility").

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "The cleft structures are appearing with genuine control — you're using them at the right rhetorical moment, not just because the task demands it. That deliberateness is a strong C1 marker. To move toward C2: (1) try deploying a cleft pair within one paragraph — state a position with an it-cleft, then dismantle it with a negative what-cleft ('It was X they claimed — but what the evidence actually shows is Y'); (2) read editorial writing specifically to notice where professional writers use clefts, then consciously replicate those patterns."

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
Example table for Rhetoric & Persuasion:
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | A speech was persuasive | A speech that invoked both ethos and emotional appeal proved cogent in unexpected ways |
| When | last year | during a pivotal public debate, when opinion was already polarised |
| Where | (not mentioned) | in a high-stakes forum where the audience was openly sceptical |
| Why | the speaker was good | because what the speaker did was presuppose shared values before making the case |
| Who | (not mentioned) | the speaker, whose credibility and rhetorical control were both decisive factors |
| How | by being persuasive | by using it-cleft structures to isolate the core argument and rhetorical questions to create a sense of inevitability |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"It was not the speaker's credentials alone that swayed the room — what proved decisive was her ability to presuppose shared values before making the case. Be that as it may, her rhetoric was not without its fallacious moments: in no small measure, the emotional appeals undercut the otherwise cogent core of her argument."

**Langkah 5 — Discourse Markers:**
Best-fitting discourse markers for Rhetoric & Persuasion (C1 level):
- **be that as it may** → "Be that as it may, the fallacious reasoning at the heart of the speech undermined its credibility."
- **in no small measure** → "The campaign's success was due, in no small measure, to the speaker's mastery of ethos."
- **insofar as** → "Insofar as rhetoric is concerned, it is the cleft sentence that signals deliberate rhetorical control."

**Langkah 6 — Craft & Lexical Chunks:**
*(Lihat PROMPT block — Kak Ara menyiapkan lexical chunks dan craft feedback spesifik topik hari ini.)*

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Flag any register inconsistencies — formal/informal mismatch or domain tone mismatch. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why. ✅ skip if consistent.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Question #1 models an impersonal construction, priming the user to respond with cleft-style structures. Question #3 combines an inverted conditional (Day 1 retrieval) with rhetoric vocabulary — multi-day retrieval practice in a single question.

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Encouraging but native-like-direct. "Your it-cleft in sentence 4 reads exactly like something from a well-written op-ed — that level of structural deliberateness is genuinely C1." "The what-cleft is close — just drop the 'to' after 'was' and it reads perfectly."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. Missing "that/who" connector in it-cleft
2. Tense mismatch: "it is" for past events
3. "to + infinitive" instead of bare infinitive after "what + subject + did/does + was"
4. Confusing "invoke" (appeal to) with "evoke" (bring to mind)
5. Overusing cleft in every sentence — register control means knowing when NOT to use it

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Strong work, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]! The cleft sentences are appearing at exactly the right moments — that's the real C1 shift. Anyone can memorise the formula; what you're doing is deploying it as a rhetorical tool, not a grammar exercise. Keep analysing how persuasion works — reading editorial writing with this lens is one of the fastest routes to C2."

**Saran Naik Level (C1 → C2):**
"For C2, practise the two-cleft counter-argument: state the opponent's position with an it-cleft ('It was X that they argued'), then dismantle it with a what-cleft ('But what the evidence actually shows is Y'). This move is a hallmark of sophisticated academic and journalistic writing."

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is in a thoughtful, semi-formal discussion — like being interviewed for a media criticism podcast — about a speech, debate, or piece of writing they've analysed. Reflective and analytical tone.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. Do you think rhetoric has become more or less effective in the era of social media — where attention spans are shorter and audiences are more sceptical?
2. Is there a speaker or writer whose ethos you find particularly persuasive, and what specifically about their style makes their case so cogent?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
- It-cleft: It was [FOCUS] that [REST]. → It was the final sentence that repudiated all previous objections.
- What-cleft: What [SUBJECT + VERB] was [FOCUS]. → What the speaker did was presuppose the audience's existing fears.
- Negative what-cleft: What [SUBJECT] could not do was [BARE INFINITIVE]. → What the argument could not do was rebut the core evidence.
