```
LANGKAH 2 — KOREKSI 8 LANGKAH (otomatis setelah aku kirim tulisan):

🔎 Self-Check Pertama — sebelum tabel Koreksi Writing, kalau ada SATU pola error yang paling signifikan di tulisanku (terutama: wrong tense agreement in mixed conditional; "should" inversion with past participle instead of bare infinitive; atau "in extremis" used as a pre-noun adjective), JANGAN langsung kasih jawabannya. Tandai HANYA lokasi + jenis errornya (contoh: "Quick check first — sentence 4 uses the 'should' inversion but the verb form after it isn't quite right. Want to adjust it before I run the full koreksi?"), lalu tunggu responsku dulu sebelum lanjut ke 1️⃣. Kalau tulisanku sudah ≥95% benar atau tidak ada pola error yang menonjol, lewati langkah ini dan langsung ke 1️⃣.

1️⃣ Koreksi Writing — tabel: Kalimat Asli | Kalimat yang Benar | Why (semua dalam English). TIDAK ADA kolom Catatan Bahasa Indonesia. Kalimat yang sudah ≥95% benar: tandai ✅, kolom Why isi "—".

2️⃣ Analisa BOW — cek setiap kata BOW yang aku pakai: ✅ tepat / ⚠️ belum tepat + contoh kalimat natural dalam English. Sertakan juga 1 kalimat singkat yang menyegarkan kembali 1-2 kata dari Box of Words Day 11 (vocab refresh — pilih dari: insofar as, by virtue of, ad hominem, is predicated on, it follows that, burden of proof).

3️⃣ Analisa CEFR — level tulisanku saat ini (dalam English) + apa yang sudah bagus + 2 tips konkret naik ke C2.

4️⃣ Perbandingan 5W+1H — tabel: What/Why/Where/When/Who/How (English) dari tulisanku vs versi lebih lengkap. Di bawahnya, "Enriched Paragraph" — versi tulisanku yang diperkaya, full English, register formal, TANPA translation Indonesia.

5️⃣ Discourse Markers — cek penggunaan inverted conditionals dan discourse markers (on reflection, in extremis). Jika belum, sarankan 2–3 inverted conditional structures dari BOW hari ini + contoh kalimat English yang menunjukkan bagaimana mereka menggeser register dari "if" biasa ke formal institutional.

6️⃣ Craft & Lexical Chunks — provide 2–3 high-register lexical chunks or collocations that C1+ native speakers use for Crisis Leadership (e.g. **under duress**, **managed retreat**, **proportionate response**, **in extremis**). Format: **chunk** → "example sentence." *(brief usage note)*. Check whether any were used naturally in my writing (✅). If not, suggest one to elevate the register.
If my writing is off-topic, blank, or not in English: ask me to write first; do not run Step 2.

---

7️⃣ Register/Formality Check — Flag any register inconsistencies: "should" inversion with past participle instead of bare infinitive; "in extremis" used as a pre-noun adjective; tense mismatch in mixed conditionals. Format: Original → More appropriate → Why (1 crisp sentence). ✅ skip if no issues found.
8️⃣ Speaking Challenge — 3 pertanyaan dalam English berdasarkan topik Crisis Leadership (grammar models untuk mixed dan inverted conditional dibangun ke dalam pertanyaan-pertanyaan):
**Had you been in charge during a major public crisis — real or hypothetical — what decision would you have made differently, and how might the outcome have changed?**
**Were you to face a situation where all available options carry significant risk, how would you determine which is a calculated risk worth taking, and which tips into recklessness?**
**On reflection, is there a moment in your own life where paralysis by analysis led you to miss a critical decision window? What did you learn from it?**

LANGKAH 3 — MODE SPEAKING (trigger: user aktifkan mode suara ChatGPT 🎙️ lalu bilang "Let's start speaking!"):

Ulangi Speaking Challenge satu per satu, dalam English. Langsung ke pertanyaan, jangan basa-basi.
Transkrip jawabanku dalam Bahasa Inggris walau aku campur bahasa. Koreksi dalam English. Kalau aku benar-benar stuck, JANGAN beri clue Bahasa Indonesia — beri paraphrase lebih sederhana, sinonim, atau 2 pilihan jawaban, semua dalam English.
Feedback per jawaban: versi kalimat lebih baik (level C1) + penjelasan singkat dalam English. Error kondisional → tulis pola yang benar dalam kurung italic. Contoh: *mixed conditional: If + Past Perfect clause + would + bare infinitive (present result)*, *inversion: Had + subject + only + past participle (no "if" needed)*.
Lancar → tambah 1 pertanyaan lanjutan yang menaikkan abstraksi. Macet → beri contoh kalimat pendek + pattern drill (Had [subject] only [verb-ed] / Were [subject] to [verb] / If [subject] had [verb-ed], [subject] would be [state] now).
Pujian singkat hanya di akhir sesi, tulus, native-like, tidak berlebihan.
```

---

### DAY 13 — The Anatomy of a Scandal: Media, Trust & Accountability
**Grammar Focus:** Reported Speech with Nuanced Distancing

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | allegation /ˌælɪˈɡeɪʃən/ | a claim that someone has done something wrong, typically made without proof at the time | – |
| 2 | cover-up /ˈkʌvər ʌp/ | a deliberate attempt to conceal evidence of wrongdoing or a serious error | – |
| 3 | redaction /rɪˈdækʃən/ | the removal or concealment of sensitive content from a document before it is published or disclosed | – |
| 4 | is alleged to have /ɪz əˈledʒd tə hæv/ | reported speech distancing: attributes a past claim to a source without the speaker endorsing its truth | – |
| 5 | is said to have /ɪz sed tə hæv/ | milder RS distancing: attributes information to unnamed sources, slightly less accusatory than "is alleged to have" | – |
| 6 | purportedly /pɜːˈpɔːtɪdli/ | supposedly; apparently — the speaker signals they are not verifying the claim they are reporting | – |
| 7 | ostensibly /ɒˈstensɪbli/ | on the surface; apparently so — often implies a different or hidden motive beneath the stated one | – |
| 8 | contend /kənˈtend/ | to assert or argue firmly; stronger than "claim", one step below "insist" — marks a speaker who is actively defending a position | – |
| 9 | impunity /ɪmˈpjuːnɪti/ | exemption from punishment or consequences; the ability to act without being held to account | – |
| 10 | substantiate /səbˈstænʃieɪt/ | to provide evidence that confirms or proves the truth of a claim; to back up an allegation with facts | – |
| 11 | narrative control /ˈnærətɪv kənˈtrəʊl/ | the power or ability to shape how a story is publicly framed and understood | – |
| 12 | sources close to /ˈsɔːsɪz kləʊs tə/ | journalism attribution formula: unnamed insider sources whose identity is protected | – |
| 13 | it would appear that /ɪt wʊd əˈpɪər ðæt/ | epistemic distancing phrase: "based on available evidence, it seems that..." — avoids definitive assertion | – |
| 14 | under the guise of /ˈʌndər ðə ɡaɪz ɒv/ | using a false or misleading appearance to conceal a true intent or action | – |
| 15 | without prejudice /wɪˈðaʊt ˈpredʒʊdɪs/ | without implying guilt or liability; in legal contexts, a statement protected from being used as evidence | – |

**Grammar Pendukung (C1):**
- **Reported Speech with Nuanced Distancing** — at B2, reported speech is direct: "She *said that* she would attend." At C1, journalists, analysts, and academics deploy a spectrum of distancing tools to attribute claims without endorsing them — signalling degrees of scepticism, source reliability, and epistemic caution.

  **The Distancing Spectrum (from cautious to assertive):**

  | Construction | Register Signal | Example |
  |---|---|---|
  | **it would appear that** | Careful epistemic distance — "I'm inferring this" | "It would appear that the cover-up extended further than initially alleged." |
  | **is said to have** + past inf. | Attribution to unnamed sources — mild | "The minister is said to have approved the redaction." |
  | **is alleged to have** + past inf. | Accusatory, unverified — legal overtone | "The official is alleged to have acted with impunity." |
  | **purportedly** + clause/phrase | Sceptical: "reportedly, though I doubt it" | "The document was purportedly leaked by a source close to the investigation." |
  | **ostensibly** + phrase | Implies hidden motive | "The inquiry was ostensibly about transparency — but sources close to the panel contend otherwise." |
  | **X contends/maintains/asserts** | Active attribution — speaker on record | "The defendant contends that the allegation was fabricated." |
  | **under the guise of** | Implies deception | "The cover-up proceeded under the guise of protecting national security." |

- **Why distancing matters at C1**: B2 uses "according to" and "reportedly." C1 uses the above spectrum to encode *how reliable* the source is, *how much* the speaker endorses the claim, and *what kind of evidence* would be needed to substantiate it. The verb you choose (contend vs allege vs maintain vs assert) changes the meaning as much as the content.

- **Common B2 → C1 upgrade:**
  - B2: "According to the journalist, the minister knew about the cover-up." (neutral attribution)
  - C1: "Sources close to the investigation allege that the minister **is said to have** authorised the cover-up — a claim he contends is without substance." (distancing + active denial + verb precision)

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
Distancing constructions in reported speech are the grammar of accountability journalism, legal reporting, and institutional analysis. They appear every time a writer must report a claim without endorsement — because the evidence is unverified, the source protected, or the legal risk of direct assertion too great. At C1, understanding this spectrum allows writers to read between the lines of quality journalism and reproduce the same precision in their own analytical writing.

---

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📖 Mode Cerita:**
A journalistic or analytical account of a real or fictional scandal — examining how it unfolded, who was involved, and what was revealed or concealed. The account should use the distancing constructions as they would appear in quality journalism — not translated from Indonesian, but thought in English.
Example: "It would appear that the cover-up had been orchestrated under the guise of a routine security review. Sources close to the inquiry contend that the key documents were heavily redacted before any independent body could assess them. The official at the centre of the allegations is said to have acted with considerable impunity throughout, ostensibly in compliance with protocol — a claim that even his own allies now struggle to substantiate."
Write 8–10 sentences analysing a real or fictional scandal — how it was exposed, what was concealed, and what the public eventually learned. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words, at least 2 distancing constructions from the BOW (is alleged to have / is said to have / purportedly / ostensibly / it would appear that / under the guise of), and at least 1 contend/maintain/assert attribution.
1. ...

3. ...
4. ...
5. ...
6. ...
7. ...
8. ...
(add sentence 9 and 10 if you want)

**⚡ Mode Kilat:**
Practice distancing precision: 1 sentence per word, using the distancing constructions where the grammar allows.
- allegation: ...
- impunity: ...
- narrative control: ...
- ostensibly: ...
- under the guise of: ...

**Speaking Challenge (3 Pertanyaan):**
1. **Think of a scandal — real or fictional — that you followed closely. It would appear that narrative control was a significant factor in how the story was told. Who controlled it, and how?**
2. **When a public figure is alleged to have acted with impunity, how do you think media coverage should be calibrated — ostensibly neutral reporting, or openly adversarial journalism?**
3. **Is it ever defensible to act under the guise of a legitimate purpose — or does the deception itself, regardless of the outcome, undermine the claim without prejudice to the goal?**

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common distancing errors at C1:
1. "Is alleged to have done" vs "is alleged to do": the construction requires a **past infinitive** ("to have + past participle"): "He is alleged to have **authorised**…" ✅ vs "He is alleged to **authorise**…" ❌ — the past infinitive signals the act happened before the allegation.
2. "Ostensibly" overused as a synonym for "apparently": "ostensibly" specifically implies a gap between appearance and reality — a hidden motive or deceptive framing. "Apparently" is more neutral. If no deception is implied, use "apparently."
3. "Purportedly" misplaced: it modifies the claim being reported, not the speaker's assessment of the outcome. "The document was **purportedly** genuine" ✅ vs "He **purportedly** should have known better" ❌ — the latter conflates distancing with moral judgement.
4. "Contend" misused as a synonym for "say": "contend" implies active, often defensive argument. "He contended that he had not been informed" ✅ — but using "contend" for neutral attribution ("she contended that the weather was cold") is a register mismatch.

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
- **without prejudice**: in formal English, this phrase is most precise in legal or quasi-legal contexts ("The statement was made **without prejudice** to any future proceedings"). In broader analytical writing, it means "without this being taken as an admission of guilt." Avoid using it as a general intensifier.
- **narrative control vs narrative**: "narrative" alone describes the story. "Narrative **control**" describes the political/institutional power over how the story is told. The distinction is important in media analysis — who has it, when they lose it, and how they try to reclaim it.
- **redaction** (noun) vs **redact** (verb): "The redaction of the report" / "They chose to redact three key paragraphs." Both are correct. "Heavily redacted" is a common collocation.
- Vocab refresh from Day 12 (1-2 words): "in extremis / decisive" — e.g., "Narrative control is most crucial in extremis, when decisive action is needed to contain a story before it metastasises."

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "The distancing constructions are doing real grammatical work — 'is said to have' and 'ostensibly' signal different degrees of scepticism, and you're deploying them in the right structural positions. For C2: (1) write a paragraph where you must choose between 'is alleged to have', 'is said to have', 'is reported to have', and 'is purported to have' — for the same claim — and explain why each would change the reader's inference; (2) practise passive distancing constructions: 'It has been contended that…' / 'It remains unclear whether…' — these remove any speaker entirely and create maximum institutional distance."

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | A scandal involving a cover-up | A systemic cover-up under the guise of national security — involving redaction, impunity, and contested allegations |
| When | when it became public | at the moment narrative control was lost — when sources close to the investigation began speaking to the press |
| Where | (not mentioned) | within the institution responsible for the original cover-up, and simultaneously in the media coverage that challenged it |
| Why | wrongdoing was concealed | ostensibly to protect institutional reputation — though sources contend the real motivation was to shield specific individuals from prosecution |
| Who | those involved | the official said to have authorised the redaction; the journalists who chose to report without prejudice; the public whose trust is alleged to have been betrayed |
| How | through concealment | through heavy redaction, narrative control, and the purported use of procedural protections to act with impunity |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"It would appear that narrative control had been the institution's first priority — sources close to the inquiry contend that the most damaging documents were heavily redacted before any independent body could substantiate the allegations. The official at the centre of it is alleged to have acted with considerable impunity, ostensibly in compliance with protocol, when the evidence suggests otherwise. Under the guise of protecting sensitive information, the cover-up proceeded without prejudice to the institution's public standing — though that standing is said to have collapsed irreversibly once the first source came forward."

**Langkah 5 — Discourse Markers:**
Best-fitting distancing constructions for Media & Scandal (C1):
- **it would appear that** → introduces an evidence-based inference without commitment: "It would appear that narrative control had been prioritised over transparency from the outset."
- **is alleged to have** → formal accusatory distancing, appropriate when reporting unverified claims: "The senior figure is alleged to have authorised the redaction personally."
- **under the guise of** → encodes implied deception: "The inquiry was conducted under the guise of impartiality while sources close to it contend otherwise."

**Langkah 6 — Craft & Lexical Chunks:**
*(Lihat PROMPT block — Kak Ara menyiapkan lexical chunks dan craft feedback spesifik topik hari ini.)*

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Flag: "ostensibly" used without implied deception (should be "apparently"); "contend" for neutral attribution (should be "note/observe"); "purportedly" modifying a moral judgement instead of a reported fact. ✅ skip if consistent.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Three questions embedding the grammar naturally: Q1 uses "it would appear that" + "narrative control" to model epistemic distancing; Q2 uses "is alleged to have" + "ostensibly" to contrast reporting stances; Q3 is an ethical challenge using "under the guise of" + "without prejudice" to test the user's abstract reasoning.

---

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Analytical and precise. "'Ostensibly' is doing a lot of work here — it's not just 'apparently', it's signalling you think there's a hidden motive. That's the precision upgrade." "Watch the construction after 'is alleged to have' — it needs the past infinitive, not the simple infinitive."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. "Is alleged to do" → should be "is alleged to **have** done"
2. "Ostensibly" used neutrally, without implied deception → "apparently" is more accurate
3. "Contend" for neutral attribution (should be "state/note") → register mismatch
4. "Without prejudice" as a general intensifier → legal/formal phrase, not versatile
5. "Purportedly" placed after a moral judgement rather than a factual claim

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Excellent work, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]. The distancing constructions are not just stylistically correct — they're encoding the right degree of scepticism for each claim. 'Ostensibly' and 'is said to have' in the same paragraph shows you're working across the distancing spectrum, not just picking one phrase and repeating it. That's advanced register control."

**Saran Naik Level (C1 → C2):**
"For C2, practise maximum institutional distancing — remove the speaker entirely with: 'It has been contended that…', 'It remains to be established whether…', 'The evidence has been taken to suggest that…'. These constructions appear in the most formal journalism, public inquiry reports, and institutional communications. They create a passive epistemic frame that implies no individual is making the claim — which is precisely their power."

---

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is speaking as a journalist, analyst, or concerned citizen — discussing a public scandal, how it was reported, and what the media got right or wrong in its coverage.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. Is there a meaningful distinction between reporting an allegation "without prejudice" and giving a public figure impunity by failing to substantiate it?
2. When narrative control shifts from the institution to the press, it would appear that the public gains information — but does it gain understanding? What's the difference?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
- Is alleged to have: [Subject] is alleged to have [past infinitive phrase].
  → The official is alleged to have authorised the cover-up without informing the board.
- It would appear that: It would appear that [evidence-based inference].
  → It would appear that narrative control was prioritised long before the allegation became public.
- Under the guise of: [Action] proceeded under the guise of [false rationale].
  → The redaction proceeded under the guise of protecting sensitive information.

### DAY 14 — Cultural Relativism vs Universal Values
**Grammar Focus:** Advanced Comparative/Superlative Register

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | moral relativism /ˈmɒrəl ˈrelətɪvɪzəm/ | the view that moral judgements are not universally valid but are shaped by cultural or individual context | – |
| 2 | universalism /ˌjuːnɪˈvɜːsəlɪzəm/ | the belief that certain values, rights, or moral principles apply equally to all human beings regardless of culture | – |
| 3 | ethnocentrism /ˌeθnəʊˈsentrɪzəm/ | the tendency to evaluate other cultures by the standards and assumptions of one's own | – |
| 4 | incommensurable /ˌɪnkəˈmenʃərəbl/ | impossible to assess by a shared standard; fundamentally different in kind rather than just degree | – |
| 5 | cultural imperialism /ˈkʌltʃərəl ɪmˌpɪərɪəlɪzəm/ | the practice of imposing one culture's values on others, often by presenting them as universal rather than culturally specific | – |
| 6 | moral absolutism /ˈmɒrəl ˈæbsəluːtɪzəm/ | the position that certain moral standards are universally and unconditionally binding, regardless of culture or context | – |
| 7 | pluralism /ˈplʊərəlɪzəm/ | the view that diverse values, beliefs, and ways of life can and should coexist within a society or across cultures | – |
| 8 | non-derogable /nɒn dɪˈrɒɡəbl/ | of rights or principles: cannot be suspended, overridden, or curtailed under any circumstances | – |
| 9 | transcend /trænˈsend/ | to go beyond the limits of; to rise above — used of values or principles claimed to surpass cultural boundaries | – |
| 10 | the more X, the more Y /ðə mɔː X ðə mɔː Y/ | double comparative: expresses a proportional relationship — "The more deeply one examines the debate, the more nuanced it becomes." | – |
| 11 | the single most /ðə ˈsɪŋɡl məʊst/ | emphatic superlative: used to signal one item is uniquely pre-eminent — "the single most contested question in applied ethics" | – |
| 12 | considerably more /kənˈsɪdərəbli mɔː/ | degree-modified comparative: signals a significant, not marginal, difference — "considerably more complex than it first appears" | – |
| 13 | arguably the most /ˈɑːɡjʊəbli ðə məʊst/ | qualified superlative: concedes that other views exist while asserting dominance — "arguably the most influential framework in the debate" | – |
| 14 | the least defensible /ðə liːst dɪˈfensɪbl/ | negative superlative: "the hardest to justify" — used to dismiss a position without outright asserting it is wrong | – |
| 15 | no less than /nəʊ les ðæn/ | emphatic comparative: "just as significant as" or "at minimum" — "a challenge no less than a complete reframing of the debate" | – |

**Grammar Pendukung (C1):**
- **Advanced Comparative/Superlative Register** — B2 uses standard comparatives ("more important than", "the most significant"). At C1, writers modify comparatives with degree adverbs, use emphatic or qualified superlatives, and deploy the double comparative structure ("the more X, the more Y") to express proportional reasoning.

  **Key C1 Comparative Patterns:**

  | Pattern | Function | Example |
  |---|---|---|
  | **the more X, the more Y** | Proportional logic | "The more deeply one examines moral relativism, the more considerably more complex the universalism position becomes." |
  | **the single most** | Emphatic uniqueness | "This is arguably the single most contested question in applied ethics." |
  | **arguably the most** | Qualified assertion | "Cultural imperialism is arguably the most damaging consequence of uncritical universalism." |
  | **considerably more** | Degree modification | "Pluralism is considerably more nuanced than a simple endorsement of moral relativism." |
  | **the least defensible** | Negative superlative | "Ethnocentrism is the least defensible starting point for cross-cultural moral analysis." |
  | **no less than** | Emphatic parallel | "The challenge is no less than reconciling incommensurable frameworks of value." |

- **Why these matter at C1**: B2 comparatives are functional but flat. C1 comparatives encode degree, qualification, and logical relationship. "Cultural imperialism is **arguably the most** damaging consequence" is considerably more analytically precise than "cultural imperialism is the most damaging consequence" — because the C1 version acknowledges epistemic humility (arguably) while still asserting the position with force. That calibration is what separates C1 from B2 analytical writing.

- **Double Comparative (the more X, the more Y)**: This is the single most distinctive C1 comparative structure. It encodes a proportional relationship between two variables — widely used in philosophical and analytical English. "The more one interrogates universalism, the more one notices its ethnocentric assumptions." It is considerably more elegant than "When you think more about universalism, you notice its ethnocentric assumptions."

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
The debate between cultural relativism and universalism is arguably the most foundational in applied ethics, philosophy, and human rights discourse. It surfaces in international law, anthropology, development policy, and political philosophy. The vocabulary and grammar of this Day are not only useful for discussing this debate — they transfer to any academic or analytical context requiring comparative judgements, ranked assessments, or proportional reasoning.

---

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📖 Mode Cerita:**
A philosophical analysis of the tension between cultural relativism and universalism — examining a specific case (human rights, cultural practices, development policy) through both lenses, using comparative structures to assess their relative merits and limitations.
Example: "The more carefully one examines the universalism position, the more one notices its ethnocentric assumptions — cultural imperialism is arguably the single most damaging consequence of applying moral absolutism without reflexivity. Pluralism offers a considerably more nuanced framework, though it is no less than a complete reframing of the question to argue that all values are incommensurable."
Write 8–10 sentences exploring the tension between cultural relativism and universalism, using a specific case or example to ground your analysis. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words, at least 2 advanced comparative/superlative structures from the BOW (the more X, the more Y / the single most / arguably the most / considerably more / the least defensible / no less than), and grammar utama: Advanced Comparative/Superlative Register.

(add sentence 9 and 10 if you want)

**Speaking Challenge (3 Pertanyaan):**
1. **The more one examines universalism, the more one finds ethnocentrism embedded in its foundations. Do you agree — or is there a non-derogable core of human rights that genuinely transcends cultural specificity?**
2. **Cultural imperialism is arguably the most serious charge levelled at universalist frameworks. But is pluralism a considerably more honest approach — or does it provide cover for practices that are, by any standard, the least defensible?**
3. **Which is more dangerous: moral relativism that accepts incommensurable values without question, or moral absolutism that imposes a single framework with impunity? How would you justify your position?**

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common errors with Advanced Comparative/Superlative:
1. "The more X, the more Y" — both clauses need a comparative element: "The more one examines relativism, the more nuanced it **becomes**" ✅ vs "The more one examines relativism, the nuanced it is" ❌ — the second clause must contain a comparative adjective/adverb ("becomes more nuanced" / "the more complex").
2. "Arguably the most" misused as a hedge only: "Arguably the most important thing is to be kind" ❌ (too casual a context; this phrase is for analytical claims) vs "This is arguably the single most contested position in applied ethics" ✅.
3. Degree modifier mismatch: "considerably the most" ❌ → "considerably more" ✅ (degree adverbs like considerably modify comparative "more", not superlative "the most").
4. "No less than" as quantity only: "No less than 5 people attended" (quantity) vs "This is a challenge no less than a complete reconception of ethics" (emphatic comparison). Both are correct, but the second use (qualitative emphasis) is the C1 register target.

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
- **non-derogable**: used almost exclusively in legal and human rights contexts ("non-derogable rights" = rights that cannot be suspended even in emergency). Outside these contexts, alternatives like "inviolable" or "unconditional" may read more naturally.
- **incommensurable vs incomparable**: "incomparable" means "so excellent it cannot be compared" (positive connotation). "Incommensurable" means "impossible to measure by a common standard" (technical, neutral). In the relativism debate, "incommensurable values" is the precise term — "incomparable values" means something different.
- **transcend**: regularly followed by a direct object: "transcend cultural boundaries" / "transcend particular traditions." Also used reflexively in analytical writing: "values that transcend the framework in which they are expressed."
- Vocab refresh from Day 13 (1-2 words): "ostensibly / narrative control" — e.g., "Universalism, ostensibly the most inclusive framework, has in practice been used to assert narrative control over cross-cultural ethical debates."

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "The double comparative is elegant — 'the more X, the more Y' is being used to track a genuine proportional relationship, not just as a stylistic flourish. The qualified superlatives (arguably the most / the single most) show you understand that assertion strength can be modulated at C1. For C2: (1) combine double comparative with a qualified superlative in the same analytical sentence; (2) use 'no less than' as a rhetorical amplifier: 'The stakes are no less than the moral coherence of the entire universalist project.'"

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | Cultural relativism vs universalism | Whether non-derogable rights can transcend cultural context — the single most contested question in applied ethics |
| When | in general | increasingly urgent as global institutions assert universalist frameworks over incommensurable cultural traditions |
| Where | (not mentioned) | in international human rights law, anthropological fieldwork, and development policy — where the tension is considerably more than theoretical |
| Why | values conflict | moral absolutism, arguably the most assertive form of universalism, risks ethnocentrism; moral relativism, the least defensible when it comes to atrocity, risks paralysis |
| Who | cultures / institutions | universalist institutions (the more they assert non-derogable standards, the more resistance they encounter from pluralist frameworks) |
| How | through negotiation | through pluralism — no less than a complete reconception of how incommensurable values can coexist |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"Cultural imperialism is arguably the single most damaging consequence of uncritical universalism — the more institutions assert non-derogable rights as if they were culturally neutral, the more they embed ethnocentric assumptions into frameworks ostensibly designed to transcend them. Moral relativism, however, is considerably less satisfying as a response: the least defensible position in any ethical framework is one that accepts incommensurable values without any basis for critique. Pluralism — no less than a complete reconception of the question — offers a more honest starting point, though it, too, must reckon with the limits of what can be relativised."

**Langkah 5 — Discourse Markers:**
Comparative structures for Cultural Relativism debate:
- **The more X, the more Y** → "The more rigorously one examines moral absolutism, the more its ethnocentric foundations become apparent."
- **Arguably the most** → introduces a defended claim without asserting it as settled fact — "arguably the most influential position in contemporary applied ethics"
- **No less than** → rhetorical amplifier: "reconciling these frameworks is a challenge no less than reconceiving the foundations of international law."

**Langkah 6 — Craft & Lexical Chunks:**
*(Lihat PROMPT block — Kak Ara menyiapkan lexical chunks dan craft feedback spesifik topik hari ini.)*

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Flag: "considerably the most" (degree modifier + superlative mismatch → should be "considerably more"); "the more X, the more Y" without comparative in second clause; "non-derogable" in casual contexts where "unconditional" or "inviolable" is more natural. ✅ skip if consistent.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Three questions build in the grammar and vocabulary: Q1 uses "the more X, the more Y" + "non-derogable" + "transcend"; Q2 uses "arguably the most" + "considerably more" + "the least defensible"; Q3 draws a direct analytical comparison that requires the user to deploy comparative reasoning.

---

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Philosophically engaged. "The double comparative is tracking a real logical relationship — it's not decoration, it's argument structure. That precision is exactly what advanced analytical writing needs." "Watch the second clause in 'the more X, the more Y' — it needs its own comparative element, not just a plain adjective."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. "The more X, the nuanced it is" → second clause needs comparative: "the **more** nuanced it becomes"
2. "Considerably the most" → modifier + superlative mismatch — use "considerably more" or "the most + noun" independently
3. "Incommensurable" confused with "incomparable" — different meanings
4. "Non-derogable" used in casual contexts → more formal alternatives: "unconditional", "inviolable"
5. "Arguably the most" applied to trivial claims → reserve for strong analytical assertions

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Genuinely impressive, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]. The double comparative is doing real argument work, not just style work — that's the distinction. You're also handling 'incommensurable' and 'non-derogable' as precision vocabulary, not just impressive-sounding words. That command of register is a hallmark of C1 writing at its best."

**Saran Naik Level (C1 → C2):**
"For C2, try combining a double comparative with a qualified superlative in the same sentence — 'The more carefully one examines the universalist position, the more one recognises it as arguably the single most fraught attempt to construct a non-derogable ethical framework from culturally specific premises.' That kind of nested analytical density is characteristic of the very best academic English."

---

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is in a structured academic discussion or philosophy seminar — making and defending analytical claims about the ethics of cultural relativism, with precision and register appropriate to a postgraduate context.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. Is there a meaningful distinction between saying that certain values are non-derogable and saying they transcend culture — or are these two ways of asserting the same thing?
2. The more one reads the literature on cultural imperialism, the more one notices it is often deployed by authoritarian states to resist external scrutiny. Does that use undermine the concept's analytical validity?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
- The more X, the more Y: The more [you examine X], the more [comparative result].
  → The more one examines moral relativism, the more clearly its limits become apparent.
- Arguably the most: [Position/claim] is arguably the most [comparative adjective] [noun].
  → Ethnocentrism is arguably the most deeply embedded assumption in universalist frameworks.
- No less than: [Challenge/task] is no less than [emphatic description].
  → Reconciling pluralism with non-derogable rights is a challenge no less than reconceiving international law.

### DAY 15 — The Economics of Attention: Why We Can't Look Away
**Grammar Focus:** Nominalisation + Passive Combo

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | attention economy /əˈtenʃən ɪˈkɒnəmi/ | the framework in which human attention is treated as a finite, monetisable resource to be bought and sold | – |
| 2 | monetisation /ˌmɒnɪtaɪˈzeɪʃən/ | the process of converting a resource, behaviour, or asset into revenue — nominalisation of "monetise" | – |
| 3 | engagement /ɪnˈɡeɪdʒmənt/ | the measurable level of user interaction with digital content; the primary currency of the attention economy | – |
| 4 | algorithmic amplification /ˌælɡəˈrɪðmɪk ˌæmplɪfɪˈkeɪʃən/ | the automatic boosting of content by recommendation systems based on predicted engagement | – |
| 5 | exploitation /ˌeksplɔɪˈteɪʃən/ | the use of something for profit at another's expense — nominalisation of "exploit" | – |
| 6 | fragmentation /ˌfræɡmənˈteɪʃən/ | the splintering of attention into shorter units, or of audiences into isolated information environments — nominalisation of "fragment" | – |
| 7 | commodification /kəˌmɒdɪfɪˈkeɪʃən/ | the transformation of something previously outside the market (attention, privacy, personal data) into a tradable commodity | – |
| 8 | the proliferation of /ðə prəˌlɪfəˈreɪʃən ɒv/ | the rapid spread or multiplication of something — nominalisation pattern: "proliferate" → "the proliferation of" | – |
| 9 | the erosion of /ðər ɪˈrəʊʒən ɒv/ | the gradual wearing away or degradation of something — nominalisation pattern: "erode" → "the erosion of" | – |
| 10 | the manipulation of /ðə məˌnɪpjʊˈleɪʃən ɒv/ | deliberate exploitation or control — nominalisation pattern: "manipulate" → "the manipulation of" | – |
| 11 | is driven by /ɪz ˈdrɪvən baɪ/ | passive construction: used to identify what forces or incentives produce an outcome | – |
| 12 | has been reduced to /hæz biːn rɪˈdjuːst tə/ | passive perfect: something has been collapsed or degraded into a simpler or less valuable form | – |
| 13 | digital extractivism /ˈdɪdʒɪtl ɪkˈstræktɪvɪzəm/ | the extraction of value (attention, data, behaviour) from users without fair compensation or informed consent | – |
| 14 | compulsive /kəmˈpʌlsɪv/ | driven by an irresistible urge; used of platform-induced behaviour that users feel unable to control despite awareness | – |
| 15 | filter bubble /ˈfɪltər ˈbʌbl/ | an algorithmically constructed environment that restricts a user's information to content confirming existing beliefs | – |

**Grammar Pendukung (C1):**
- **Nominalisation** — converting verbs or adjectives into nouns to create formal, dense, analytical prose:

  | Active/Verb form (B2) | Nominalisation (C1) | In a sentence |
  |---|---|---|
  | to exploit → exploitation | the exploitation of attention | "The exploitation of attention by digital platforms has been systematically underestimated." |
  | to fragment → fragmentation | the fragmentation of focus | "The fragmentation of public discourse is driven by algorithmic amplification." |
  | to monetise → monetisation | the monetisation of engagement | "The monetisation of engagement has transformed media economics." |
  | to proliferate → proliferation | the proliferation of filter bubbles | "The proliferation of filter bubbles has deepened political fragmentation." |
  | to erode → erosion | the erosion of attention | "The erosion of sustained reading capacity has been accelerated by compulsive scrolling." |
  | to manipulate → manipulation | the manipulation of cognition | "The manipulation of cognitive vulnerability is central to the attention economy." |

- **Passive + Nominalisation Combo** — combining both in one analytical passage creates the density of high-register academic English:
  - Active (B2): "Social media companies exploit users' attention and monetise their data."
  - Nominalisation only (C1 step 1): "The exploitation of users' attention and the monetisation of personal data by social media companies..."
  - Passive only (C1 step 2): "Users' attention has been exploited and their data monetised."
  - Combo (full C1): "Human attention **has been reduced to** a monetisable commodity. **The commodification of** cognitive engagement **is driven by** the same algorithmic logic that makes filter bubbles compulsive."

- **Why this matters at C1**: Nominalisation creates analytical objectivity — the process is the subject, not the actor. "The exploitation of attention" focuses on the phenomenon; "platforms exploit attention" focuses on the accusation. Academic writing and quality journalism use this to discuss systems rather than individuals, consequences rather than intentions.

- **B2 Contrast**: B2 writing is more agent-focused and active. C1 writing shifts agency onto processes and structures. Neither is better — but the passive + nominalisation combo is the register expected in formal analysis, policy writing, and academic English.

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
The attention economy is the dominant economic model of the internet. Every digital product competes for finite human attention and monetises engagement. Understanding this vocabulary allows analytical discussion of media consumption, platform design, algorithmic bias, mental health, and political polarisation. The grammar (nominalisation + passive) is not just an attention-economy technique — it is the standard register of academic analysis across disciplines.

---

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📖 Mode Cerita:**
An analytical account of how digital platforms have changed the way humans consume information — focusing on the mechanisms of the attention economy and the consequences for individual behaviour and public discourse.
Example: "Human attention **has been reduced to** a tradable resource in the digital age. **The monetisation of** engagement **is driven by** algorithmic amplification, which rewards compulsive interaction over substantive content. **The proliferation of** filter bubbles has accelerated **the fragmentation of** public discourse in ways that digital extractivism alone cannot account for."
Write 8–10 sentences analysing how the attention economy shapes your own digital behaviour or a broader social phenomenon. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words, at least 2 nominalisation patterns (the exploitation of / the erosion of / the proliferation of / the manipulation of / etc.) and at least 1 passive + nominalisation combo. Grammar utama: Nominalisation + Passive Combo.
1. ...
2. ...
3. ...
4. ...
5. ...
6. ...
7. ...
8. ...
(add sentence 9 and 10 if you want)

**⚡ Mode Kilat:**
Convert each sentence from active voice + verb form into a formal academic sentence using nominalisation (and passive where natural):
- attention economy: ...
- commodification: ...
- the erosion of: ...
- algorithmic amplification: ...
- filter bubble: ...

**Speaking Challenge (3 Pertanyaan):**
1. **The commodification of attention has been driven by the monetisation of engagement. Do you experience this in your own digital behaviour — and if so, what does that experience of compulsive platform use feel like from the inside?**
2. **The proliferation of filter bubbles is driven by algorithmic amplification rather than user choice. In your view, is the erosion of shared information environments a form of digital extractivism — or simply the consequence of individual preference?**
3. **If human attention has been reduced to a commodity, what responsibility — if any — falls on the individual user, and what has been displaced onto the platform by the very design of the engagement economy?**

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common nominalisation and passive errors at C1:
1. **Incomplete nominalisation**: "The proliferation of social media is bad" — nominalisation without analytical follow-through → pair it with what the proliferation does: "The proliferation of social media has accelerated the fragmentation of public attention." (nominalisation → consequence)
2. **Passive without agent**: "The data has been monetised" — correct but incomplete. C1 passive typically indicates *by whom* or *through what mechanism*: "Personal data has been monetised through engagement-tracking algorithms."
3. **Nominalisation overload**: stacking too many nominalisations in one sentence creates unreadable prose. Maximum 2-3 per sentence: "The commodification of the exploitation of the fragmentation of..." → split into two sentences.
4. **"Is driven by" + agent confusion**: "Engagement **is driven by** the user's desire" ✅ vs "Engagement **is driven by** we scroll compulsively" ❌ — "is driven by" requires a noun phrase, not a clause.

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
- **engagement** (in digital context): differs from its general use ("his engagement with the audience"). In the attention economy, "engagement" is a technical metric (clicks, comments, shares, watch time). Write "digital engagement" or "online engagement" if the context might be ambiguous.
- **digital extractivism**: a deliberate reference to resource extractivism (mining, oil drilling) — implying that platforms extract user value the way colonial economies extracted raw materials. It encodes a critical political economy perspective.
- **filter bubble vs echo chamber**: "filter bubble" = what the algorithm does to you (restricts what you see). "Echo chamber" = what you choose (you seek confirming voices). Both are relevant, but at C1 the distinction matters.
- **compulsive** (adjective): "compulsive behaviour", "compulsive scrolling", "compulsive use" — always describes behaviour patterns, not platform design itself ("compulsive platform" ❌).
- Vocab refresh from Day 14 (1-2 words): "the more X, the more Y / ethnocentrism" — e.g., "The more deeply one examines the attention economy, the more clearly the commodification of human cognition becomes apparent — arguably a new form of cultural imperialism, ethnocentric in its assumption that engagement metrics transcend cultural difference."

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "The nominalisation is doing real academic work — 'the erosion of sustained attention' is considerably more analytical than 'attention is getting worse', because it names the process, not just the outcome. For C2: (1) use nominalisation chains strategically — 'the commodification of the monetisation process' to show nested causality; (2) write a paragraph using only passive-nominalisation constructions to describe the same phenomenon, then rewrite with entirely active sentences — compare which is more precise and which is more vivid."

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | Social media takes up too much of my time | The compulsive engagement patterns have been produced by the systematic monetisation of attention through algorithmic amplification |
| When | all the time | continuously, insofar as the engagement economy is designed to eliminate any natural break point |
| Where | on my phone | within an attention economy where filter bubbles have been constructed algorithmically |
| Why | it is addictive | the commodification of engagement is driven by profit; compulsive use has been deliberately engineered through exploitation of cognitive vulnerability |
| Who | me / platforms | the user whose attention has been monetised; the platforms whose architecture is driven by the proliferation of engagement metrics |
| How | scrolling | through the erosion of sustained attention, the algorithmic amplification of outrage, and digital extractivism on a scale previously unimaginable |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"Human attention **has been reduced to** a monetisable resource — the primary asset of an economy **driven by** engagement rather than meaning. **The commodification of** digital behaviour **is driven by** algorithmic amplification, which rewards compulsive interaction and systematically suppresses content requiring sustained focus. **The erosion of** reading comprehension and public deliberation **has been accelerated by** the very architecture of the platforms that profit from it. **The proliferation of** filter bubbles is not an accident of digital extractivism — it is, arguably, its most effective mechanism."

**Langkah 5 — Discourse Markers:**
Nominalisation + Passive patterns for Attention Economy analysis:
- **The [process] of [noun] has been [past participle] by [agent]** → "The monetisation of engagement has been accelerated by algorithmic amplification."
- **[Abstract noun] is driven by** → "The proliferation of filter bubbles is driven by the same logic that makes compulsive scrolling profitable."
- **Has been reduced to** → marks degradation/transformation: "Human attention has been reduced to a unit of tradable data."

**Langkah 6 — Craft & Lexical Chunks:**
*(Lihat PROMPT block — Kak Ara menyiapkan lexical chunks dan craft feedback spesifik topik hari ini.)*

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Flag: nominalisation overload (more than 3 chained nominalisations per sentence); passive without agent or mechanism; "is driven by" followed by a clause instead of a noun phrase; "compulsive" applied to platform design instead of user behaviour. ✅ skip if consistent.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Q1 is concrete and personal — monetisation + compulsive from the inside. Q2 is analytical — proliferation + algorithmic amplification + erosion as a system. Q3 is philosophical — personal responsibility vs design intent — requiring comparatives and conditional reasoning built on the Day's vocabulary.

---

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Analytically precise. "'The erosion of sustained attention' is better than 'attention is getting worse' — it names the process and implies it is gradual, systematic, and measurable. That precision is the C1 upgrade." "Nominalisation is powerful but dangerous in excess — two or three chained nominalisations in one sentence and it becomes unreadable. One well-placed nominalisation beats three weak ones."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. Nominalisation without consequence ("the proliferation of social media is bad" → what did it do?)
2. Passive without agent or mechanism
3. Nominalisation overload (3+ chained nominalisations)
4. "Is driven by" followed by a clause instead of a noun phrase
5. "Compulsive" applied to a platform rather than to user behaviour

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Really well done, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]. The nominalisation is analytical, not just stylistic — 'the commodification of engagement' is telling me what process occurred, what it acted on, and where. That's the C1 nominalisation standard. The passive + nominalisation combo reads like quality academic English throughout."

**Saran Naik Level (C1 → C2):**
"For C2, try what's sometimes called 'nominalisation embedding' — a nominalisation as the subject of a passive sentence that itself contains another nominalisation: 'The commodification of human attention has been accelerated by the proliferation of algorithmic engagement incentives.' Three nominalisations — subject, object, instrument — and still readable because they're properly distributed. That density is a C2 signature."

---

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is speaking as a media analyst, digital ethicist, or concerned platform user — explaining the attention economy to a thoughtful non-expert audience with precision and register.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. Has the monetisation of engagement changed *what* we find interesting — or only *how often* we seek it? Is there a meaningful distinction?
2. Digital extractivism implies that value is being removed from users without consent. But users have often chosen to participate. Does informed participation dissolve the critique — or is the manipulation of choice itself the problem?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
- Nominalisation: the [verb → noun] of [object] has [passive verb] by [agent].
  → The monetisation of personal data has been accelerated by the attention economy's incentive structure.
- Is driven by: [Phenomenon] is driven by [underlying force].
  → The proliferation of filter bubbles is driven by engagement metrics, not user demand.
- Has been reduced to: [Subject] has been reduced to [degraded description].
  → Human attention has been reduced to a unit of digital inventory.

### DAY 16 — Genetic Engineering & the Boundaries of Ethics
**Grammar Focus:** Subjunctive + Epistemic Modal Combo

#### 📚 Detail Materi

**Target Kosakata (Box of Words):**

| No | Kosakata + Phonetic UK | English Definition | Catatan Indonesia |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | germline modification /ˈdʒɜːmlaɪn ˌmɒdɪfɪˈkeɪʃən/ | genetic changes made to egg, sperm, or embryo cells — these modifications are heritable and passed to all future generations | – |
| 2 | enhancement /ɪnˈhɑːnsmənt/ | improving a human trait beyond its normal functioning — ethically and legally distinct from therapeutic treatment | – |
| 3 | hubris /ˈhjuːbrɪs/ | arrogant overconfidence in human capability; the assumption that biotechnology can safely override natural systems without risk | – |
| 4 | eugenics /juːˈdʒenɪks/ | the discredited ideology of controlling human reproduction to supposedly improve the population — now applied critically to genetic enhancement debates | – |
| 5 | bioethics /ˌbaɪəʊˈeθɪks/ | the systematic study of ethical issues arising from advances in biology, medicine, and biotechnology | – |
| 6 | moratorium /ˌmɒrəˈtɔːriəm/ | a temporary, agreed suspension of an activity, pending further research, review, or regulation | – |
| 7 | off-target effect /ˈɒf ˈtɑːɡɪt ɪˈfekt/ | in genetic engineering: unintended modification to regions of the genome other than the intended target | – |
| 8 | unintended consequence /ˌʌnɪnˈtendɪd ˈkɒnsɪkwəns/ | an outcome not anticipated when an intervention was planned — the central risk in complex biological and social systems | – |
| 9 | it is vital that [bare verb] /ɪt ɪz ˈvaɪtl ðæt/ | mandative subjunctive: "It is vital that oversight **be** maintained." — the verb is bare infinitive (not "is maintained") | – |
| 10 | cannot be ruled out /ˈkænɒt biː ruːld aʊt/ | epistemic negation: a possibility that remains open and cannot be excluded — "Off-target effects cannot be ruled out." | – |
| 11 | has yet to be established /hæz jet tə biː ɪˈstæblɪʃt/ | epistemic: not yet proven, demonstrated, or confirmed — "Long-term safety has yet to be established." | – |
| 12 | it is paramount that [bare verb] /ɪt ɪz ˈpærəmaʊnt ðæt/ | mandative subjunctive, stronger degree: "It is paramount that all trials **be** independently reviewed." (bare verb, not "are reviewed") | – |
| 13 | is liable to /ɪz ˈlaɪəbl tə/ | epistemic: likely to; prone to under certain conditions — "Any enhancement programme is liable to be misused." | – |
| 14 | it should be noted that /ɪt ʃʊd biː ˈnəʊtɪd ðæt/ | epistemic discourse marker: formally introduces an important caveat or qualification | – |
| 15 | we recommend that [bare verb] /wiː ˌrekəˈmend ðæt/ | mandative subjunctive: formal recommendation — "We recommend that all germline trials **be** suspended." (bare verb, not "are suspended") | – |

**Grammar Pendukung (C1):**
- **Mandative Subjunctive** — after verbs/adjectives of necessity, recommendation, or demand, the clause that follows uses the **bare infinitive** (subjunctive mood), not the indicative. This is standard in formal, academic, and institutional English:

  | Trigger Word/Phrase | Subjunctive Form | Indicative (B2/informal) |
  |---|---|---|
  | It is vital that | oversight **be** independent | oversight **is** independent |
  | It is paramount that | trials **be** suspended | trials **are** suspended |
  | We recommend that | the committee **review** the data | the committee **reviews** the data |
  | It is necessary that | consent **be** obtained | consent **is** obtained |
  | The board insists that | the moratorium **remain** in place | the moratorium **remains** in place |

  The bare infinitive applies to **all persons** — including third person singular: "It is vital that the regulation **be** updated" (not "be**s**").

- **Epistemic Modals (C1 cluster for science/ethics)** — express degrees of probability, uncertainty, and evidential status. The cluster used in Bioethics writing:

  | Expression | Epistemic Force | Example |
  |---|---|---|
  | **cannot be ruled out** | Non-excludable possibility | "Eugenics-adjacent uses cannot be ruled out." |
  | **has yet to be established** | Currently unproven | "Safety at germline level has yet to be established." |
  | **is liable to** | Probabilistic tendency | "Unchecked enhancement is liable to replicate existing inequalities." |
  | **it should be noted that** | Important caveat | "It should be noted that no long-term off-target data exists." |

- **Combo (Subjunctive + Epistemic Modal)**: high-register bioethics/policy writing combines both in the same paragraph — the subjunctive makes recommendations; the epistemic modals acknowledge uncertainty:
  "It is paramount that germline modification **be** subject to international oversight. It should be noted that off-target effects cannot be ruled out, and long-term safety has yet to be established. Enhancement applications are liable to generate eugenic pressures that a simple moratorium may be insufficient to contain."

- **B2 → C1 contrast:**
  - B2: "We need to make sure this is controlled carefully." 
  - C1 Subjunctive: "It is paramount that this **be** subject to rigorous independent control."
  - C1 Epistemic: "The long-term consequences cannot be ruled out and have yet to be established."

**Konteks Penggunaan:**
Genetic engineering raises questions that sit at the intersection of science, ethics, law, and philosophy. The mandative subjunctive is the grammar of formal recommendation — how international bodies, ethics committees, and policy papers phrase their conclusions. The epistemic modals are the grammar of scientific uncertainty — how responsible scientists and analysts frame claims where the evidence is incomplete. Together, they constitute the register of serious bioethical discourse.

---

#### ✅ Detail Task

**📖 Mode Cerita:**
A bioethical analysis of a real or hypothetical case of genetic engineering — examining what should be regulated, what risks exist, and what the ethics of enhancement versus treatment looks like in practice.
Example: "It is vital that germline modification **be** approached with a degree of humility rarely seen in technological development — hubris has historically preceded the most catastrophic unintended consequences. It should be noted that off-target effects cannot be ruled out under current methodology, and the long-term safety of such modifications has yet to be established. A moratorium is not an overreaction; it is, arguably, the only proportionate response to a field whose epistemological assumptions are liable to exceed its actual capabilities."
Write 8–10 sentences analysing the ethics of genetic engineering, enhancement, or a specific application of biotechnology. Use at least 5 words from the Box of Words, at least 2 mandative subjunctive constructions (it is vital that / it is paramount that / we recommend that), and at least 2 epistemic modals (cannot be ruled out / has yet to be established / is liable to / it should be noted that). Grammar utama: Subjunctive + Epistemic Modal Combo.
1. ...
2. ...
3. ...
4. ...
5. ...
6. ...
7. ...
8. ...
(add sentence 9 and 10 if you want)

**⚡ Mode Kilat:**
1 formal sentence per word below — include at least 1 mandative subjunctive and 1 epistemic modal across your 5 sentences:
- germline modification: ...
- hubris: ...
- moratorium: ...
- off-target effect: ...
- eugenics: ...

**Speaking Challenge (3 Pertanyaan):**
1. **It is vital that genetic enhancement be regulated at an international level — but it should be noted that international agreements are notoriously difficult to enforce. What realistic mechanism would you propose?**
2. **The distinction between treatment and enhancement cannot be ruled out as being culturally constructed — what counts as "normal" is liable to shift over time. Does this undermine the ethical case for a moratorium on enhancement?**
3. **Eugenics has yet to be fully reckoned with as part of the history of medicine. In light of that history, how should bioethics approach genetic engineering — with openness, or with a degree of principled suspicion?**

---

#### 🔍 Detail Review & Koreksi (8 Langkah)

**Langkah 1 — Koreksi Writing:**
Common errors with Subjunctive + Epistemic Modal:
1. **Forgetting the subjunctive after "vital/paramount/recommend"**: "It is vital that oversight **is** maintained" ❌ → "It is vital that oversight **be** maintained" ✅ — the subjunctive uses the bare infinitive, not the present indicative.
2. **Third person singular with subjunctive**: "It is essential that the committee **reviews** the data" ❌ → "It is essential that the committee **review** the data" ✅ — no "-s" in the subjunctive, even for third person singular.
3. **"Is liable to" + noun instead of verb**: "The programme is liable to misuse" ❌ → "The programme is liable to **be misused**" ✅ (or: "The programme is liable to **result in** misuse") — "is liable to" is always followed by an infinitive, not a noun directly.
4. **"Has yet to be established" used for abstract philosophical claims**: reserve for empirically testable claims — "Whether gene editing is ethical has yet to be established" ❌ (ethics is not empirically established) → "Whether the long-term safety is acceptable has yet to be established" ✅.

**Langkah 2 — Analisa BOW:**
- **hubris vs arrogance**: "arrogance" is a character flaw; "hubris" (from Greek tragedy) implies a specific overconfidence that invites catastrophic reversal — a cosmic punishment for exceeding human limits. In bioethics, "hubris" is the stronger, more precise term: it implies that the overreach itself will generate its own undoing.
- **eugenics**: a loaded term. Always apply critically — not descriptively. "Enhancement advocates have been accused of reviving eugenic assumptions" ✅ vs "gene editing is a form of eugenics" — the latter may overstate the comparison. Use with precision.
- **moratorium vs ban**: "moratorium" = temporary suspension pending review (allows resumption). "Ban" = permanent prohibition. These are not synonymous. "A moratorium on germline trials" is a far less absolute recommendation than "a ban on germline trials."
- **unintended consequence**: an established compound — write as two separate words (not hyphenated). "The law of unintended consequences" is a related idiom.
- Vocab refresh from Day 15 (1-2 words): "the erosion of / has been reduced to" — e.g., "The erosion of the treatment/enhancement distinction has been accelerated by technological capability, and the moral framework around bioethics has yet to be established to match it."

**Langkah 3 — Analisa CEFR:**
Template: "The mandative subjunctive is being deployed correctly — 'it is vital that oversight be maintained' reads as genuinely formal institutional English, not a B2 paraphrase. The epistemic modals ('cannot be ruled out', 'has yet to be established') are working as hedges, which is exactly their function in the formal register of scientific analysis. For C2: (1) embed the mandative inside a conditional: 'Should the moratorium be lifted, it is paramount that independent review mechanisms be strengthened' — that stacks inverted conditional + mandative subjunctive; (2) use 'has yet to be established' in a sentence that specifies *what* would count as establishing it — that precision is C2 epistemological thinking."

**Langkah 4 — 5W+1H:**
| Elemen | Versi User | Versi Lebih Lengkap |
|---|---|---|
| What | genetic engineering and its risks | germline modification whose off-target effects cannot be ruled out and whose long-term safety has yet to be established |
| When | now | at a moment when the hubris of enhancement advocates has yet to be tempered by adequate bioethical frameworks |
| Where | (not mentioned) | in research laboratories and regulatory bodies, where it is paramount that independent oversight be mandatory |
| Why | ethical concerns | because enhancement is liable to revive eugenic pressures; because unintended consequences in heritable germline modification are literally irreversible across generations |
| Who | scientists, regulators, society | the bioethics community, which recommends that any germline trial be subject to a moratorium pending international consensus |
| How | through regulation | it is vital that international bodies be empowered to enforce a moratorium, and that enhancement be formally distinguished from therapeutic treatment |

**Enriched Paragraph:**
"The hubris embedded in uncritical genetic enhancement is arguably the single most dangerous assumption in contemporary bioethics. It should be noted that off-target effects cannot be ruled out under current methodologies, and long-term safety at the germline level has yet to be established. It is paramount that any regulatory framework **be** designed with the understanding that germline modification is heritable — that unintended consequences, unlike those in somatic interventions, cannot be undone across generations. Enhancement applications are liable to slide, incrementally and inexorably, into eugenic territory unless it is vital that the treatment/enhancement boundary **be** formally defined and independently enforced."

**Langkah 5 — Discourse Markers:**
Subjunctive + Epistemic Modal combinations for Bioethics:
- **It is vital that + bare verb** → mandative force: "It is vital that germline research **be** subject to a moratorium until safety has been established."
- **cannot be ruled out** → non-excludable epistemic: "Enhancement applications that replicate eugenic assumptions cannot be ruled out under current frameworks."
- **has yet to be established** → scientific humility marker: "The safety of off-target effects in heritable cells has yet to be established despite decades of research."

**Langkah 6 — Craft & Lexical Chunks:**
*(Lihat PROMPT block — Kak Ara menyiapkan lexical chunks dan craft feedback spesifik topik hari ini.)*

**Langkah 7 — Register/Formality Check:**
Flag: indicative "is" after "it is vital that" (should be bare infinitive "be"); "is liable to" followed by a noun instead of an infinitive; "has yet to be established" applied to non-empirical claims; "hubris" used as synonym for simple arrogance (loses its specific implication of overreach-inviting-reversal). ✅ skip if consistent.

**Langkah 8 — Speaking Challenge:**
Q1 embeds the subjunctive and "it should be noted that" into the question itself. Q2 uses "cannot be ruled out" and "is liable to" to model epistemic hedging. Q3 uses "has yet to be" to frame an ongoing historical and moral reckoning, requiring the user to reason about precaution and history simultaneously.

---

#### 💬 Detail Feedback & Panduan Kak Ara

**Tone & Bahasa:**
Careful and intellectually serious. "'It is paramount that the framework be independent' — that subjunctive is doing a lot of work. It marks this as a formal recommendation, not a preference. The precision in 'cannot be ruled out' vs 'is likely to' matters — the first is an epistemic door that can't be closed; the second is a probability estimate." "Watch the subjunctive after 'vital/paramount/recommend' — the bare infinitive is the rule, no exceptions, not even for third person singular."

**Error Umum Topik Ini:**
1. "It is vital that it **is** maintained" → must be "**be** maintained" (bare infinitive)
2. Third person singular "-s" in subjunctive → no "-s" even for he/she/it
3. "Is liable to" + noun directly → needs infinitive after "to"
4. "Has yet to be established" for abstract/philosophical claims → reserve for empirically testable propositions
5. "Hubris" used as neutral synonym for arrogance → loses its specific meaning of overreach-inviting-downfall

**Template Pujian (Akhir Sesi):**
"Excellent, [PANGGILAN] [NAMA]. The subjunctive is appearing in exactly the right contexts — formal recommendation with genuine institutional authority. The epistemic hedges are doing what they should: acknowledging uncertainty without abandoning the analytical claim. This is bioethics writing at a level that reads like a published policy brief."

**Saran Naik Level (C1 → C2):**
"For C2, try embedding the mandative inside a conditional: 'Should the moratorium be lifted, it is paramount that independent review mechanisms **be** strengthened before any germline trial **be** approved.' That stacks an inverted conditional + two mandative subjunctives in one sentence — complex but entirely natural in the highest register of institutional English."

---

#### 🗣️ Detail Practice (Speaking Mode)

**Skenario Speaking:**
The user is participating in a bioethics panel or policy discussion — expected to make and defend regulatory recommendations about genetic engineering with precision, epistemic humility, and institutional-register English.

**Pertanyaan Lanjutan (jika user lancar):**
1. It has been suggested that the treatment/enhancement distinction is itself a moral construct rather than a scientific fact. Were this argument to be accepted, would it follow that a moratorium based on that distinction is also liable to collapse?
2. Is there a risk that a moratorium on genetic enhancement — while it is vital that safety be established — might itself have unintended consequences, such as concentrating research in jurisdictions where oversight is weaker?

**Pattern Drill (jika user macet):**
- Mandative subjunctive: It is [vital/paramount/necessary] that [subject] [bare infinitive].
  → It is paramount that all germline research be subject to independent oversight.
- Cannot be ruled out: [Claim/risk] cannot be ruled out [under/without] [condition].
  → Off-target effects at germline level cannot be ruled out under existing protocols.
- Has yet to be established: [Safety/evidence/consensus] has yet to be established [on/regarding] [subject].
  → Long-term safety of heritable modifications has yet to be established across multiple generations.
